理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	richard resnick: welcome to the gene revolution .

如果猜對的話我們就可以在六維載荷空間中構造標準載荷集作為更完美的七維載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集	if we guess correctly , we can construct standard charges in six charge dimensions as a perfect concentration of sevendimensional charges .
這種粒子選擇方法由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年提出它是大統一理論的一種探索	this particular choice of particles , proposed by patty and salam in 1973 , a unified theory of grand unification .
在我們看到這個新的合成圖案時發現有些空間應該有粒子卻空出來了	when we look at this new synthesis pattern , we see that there are spaces where particles are supposed to be empty .
這是統一理論的研究方式	this is how the idea of unification works .
物理學家將已有的結構作為子集探索更大更對稱的結構	physicists explore larger , more symmetrical structures as subsets .
這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this larger configuration allows us to predict the particles that actually exist but aren’t seen .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification model suggests that these two new particles should be very similar to the weak force , but weakened .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now you can rotate this charge in seven dimensions , and consider the odd effects of particles: the second and third generations of matter in sixdimensional charge space have the same charges as the first generation .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can’t be identified by their six charges .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	they overlay each other in the standard charge space .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	however , in eightdimensional charge space , we can assign unique new charges to each particle .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then rotate in eight dimensions and see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second and third generations of matter associated with a symmetry , called the triality , associated with the first generation .
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular pattern of charges in eightdimensional is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exceptional lie group of e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	this lie group is a smooth , curved , 248dimensional space .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	each point in this image will find a symmetry in this beautiful , complicated , beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a small portion of e8 can be used to describe the distortion of einstein's theory of general relativity , explaining gravity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	this geometry , along with quantum mechanics , is capable of describing things at the smallest scales .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and in this pattern of eightdimensional charge space , it appears to be beautiful , and it also includes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just one of the surfaces of this complicated shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	as you spin it , you can see a lot of intricate patterns contained in them .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	and through some kind of spin , we can look down through the 8dimensional space along a symmetry axis and look at all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a beautiful structure , and like any other unification theory , we can see that some of the holes are needed for new particles to fill in this pattern .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	in this gap , 20 new particles need new particles to fill , two of which have been filled by pat and salaam particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	from the position of the pattern , we know that these new particles are like the higgs particles in a quantum field , but they have color charge and interact with strong forces .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	filling in these new particles completed the pattern , giving us the full e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	in the mathematics world , it's considered the most beautiful structure .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	some people have proposed that this structure with this incredible beauty can describe the truth about the interaction of particles at the very smallest scales we can imagine .
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematically describes a natural theory is not just new .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " this book of nature has been written in front of us us us using mathematical language .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it's made of triangular circles and other geometrical shapes that don't have these things that are humanly impossible to understand without these things we're going to be lost in a dark labyrinth . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i believe this is true , and i've tried to follow galileo's instructions , describing the mathematics of quantum physics by triangles and other geometries .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	when other physicists and i study these things , mathematics is like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we believe at the heart of mathematics is a beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	together , mathematics and quantum mechanics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , while particles interact in each position , revealing a beautiful pattern .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	furthermore , we may see an e8 pattern , or an e8 pattern , of the large hadron collider , reflecting the nature .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	the discovery process is an amazing adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit the e8 pattern , that's very cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc finds new particles but doesn't fit this pattern , it's going to be really interesting , although it's bad for e8 theory .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and to some extent , it was bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	how bad would it be ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's very bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but predicting how nature works is always risky .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	the theory , and the other theories about this , are focused .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	although it takes a lot of energy to acquire a lot of fruit , it doesn't necessarily appe
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	theoretical physics is a very common thing to fail .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	in this regard , new physics theories are like startup companies .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	it's always hard to get emotionally broken when investing in something that doesn't work .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it doesn't work , you have to throw it away and try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in all of these uncertainties is to keep balance and perspective in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've kept my balance as much as i could .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i'm trying to balance my physics , love and surfing , and that's where my charges are .
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	so even if my physics studies weren't working , i would still have a good life .

年紀小的黑猩猩花很長時間觀察它們的長輩做什麼	these young chimpanzees spend a lot of time observing what their elders do .
我們現在知道 , 他們能模仿所見的行為表現	we now know that they can mimic what they're seeing .
我們認為正是由此從那些在非洲研究的所有不同黑猩猩種群身上看到的使用工具的不同行為這些行為是怎樣透過觀察、模仿和實踐從一代傳到另一代的所以 , 我們可以把這些使用工具的行為說成是原始文化	and we think it's the evidence that we're doing all the different behaviors that we see in chimpanzee groups in africa , how that behavior is through observation , emulation and practice , from generation to generation , so we can think of these tool behaviors as being primitive culture .
黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees don't have a language , we mentioned it .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have an entirely rich set of gestures and motions , many of which are very similar to ours , or even identical , and have the same inclusion that chimpanzees hug when they say hello .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they also kiss , hold hands , pat one on the other .
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also bluffing , scare or rocks .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzees' societies , we find a lot of compassion , demonstrations , and real examples .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	like us , unfortunately , they also have the dark side of their nature .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be incredibly revereling , even like a prototype war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	in most cases , these extremely aggressive behaviors are directly related to individuals within a neighboring community .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of these attacks would be to compete for the plate .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's helpful for us to recognize that the rest of humans and other members of the animal kingdom are at the boundaries .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	it's a very ambiguous line , and as more of our observations keep getting more ambiguous .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	my work began in 1960 , and it's been going on .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	these chimpanzees lived in complex social life in the wild , and most importantly , they helped us to realize that we live with a shaped animal on the planet , and we are part of the brain that can't be separated from these animals .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find that chimpanzees , as many other creatures around the world , have lost their habitat .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a picture from the air , and you can see the gombe highlands covered by the forest .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	i walked the country over 16 years ago and realized that outside of the park , this forest spreads across the east coast of tanganyika in 1960 , and it's a kind of inextinctive , 30 square miles of gombe national park , which sits here , and there's a problem in my head .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we go in and try to save the famous chimpanzees , and the people who live around the national park are struggling for survival ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people , not just land , that can afford it .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	as refugees from burundi poured into people from the congo , over lakes , more people live there .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those people are very poor , can't buy it from elsewhere .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	this is a project that we call " love . "
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's an integrated way to improve the lives of people who live in the villages around the villages .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	first it was small , it had 12 villages . it's 24 .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there isn't time to go into it , but it's a project of things like forest raised beds , and for the mountains , this method that's currently eroding a significant desert land , multiple farming species .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	control , prevent land eroding .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	the overused agricultural fields were recycled in less than two years , and they were recycled .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	helping the villagers to get fresh water from wells .
或許建一些校舍	maybe we could build some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think the most important part of this is working with smallscale groups of women , giving them the tiny credit rates .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	we've received about 95 percent of all the loans in the world .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	this allows women to be educated , give scholarships to girls so they can finish secondary school , knowing that the level of education that women around the world have fallen their families .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we are providing information about planning and birth control and hiv/aids .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	something happened naturally after the project was implemented .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what happened in the protection is that farmers who lived in these 24 villages did not look at us as part of a whole bunch of monkeys , by the way , a lot of white men , who are now tanzanians , and when we started this program in the village , it was a tanzanian group .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	talking to the villagers was a tanzanian team asking what interested the villagers .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in natural protection ? it's not at all clear .
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health . they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	over time , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand more of the need for conservation .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher positions on the mountain were cut , the horrible land eroded and muddy came .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now we're developing what we call the biggmbe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is a region outside the national park that includes all these landscapes .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	and since these villages are standards that are higher , they actually agree to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on the higher side of the earth to have the trees growing back again , the chimps will have green corridors that allow them to cultivate through their genes to interact with the rest of the park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so love succeeds .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we reproduce this program in other parts of africa , in other parts of the world , against the wilderness of the extreme population pressure .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , like all the things we've been talking about here at ted all these days , africa's problems are a major problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's very poor .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	there are plenty of people who live on less fertile land , especially when you take the trees and you cut the soil bare winds away , and the people who are in despair eat more and more trees so that they can work to cultivate food for themselves and their families , and what will happen then ? some will start sacrificing them .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	there's another question not just in africa but all the other developing world , and even anywhere on earth what are we doing to our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	the famous scientist , e . o . wilson , said that if every standard of life on earth reaches europe , we need three more planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say four . we don't have one . we have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what happened ? i mean , the problem here is , we might have been calling perhaps the most intelligent life on earth , the most intelligent brains , with these ted conferences , but we're destroying this extraordinary home .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	indigenous peoples all over the world are sitting together before they make important decisions , and asking , " how does this affect our next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , critical decisions i'm not talking about in africa , but the fact that the world , with millions of dollars in it , and the important decisions of millions of people , are just asking , " how does that affect the next shareholder's meeting ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	as i began to travel over africa talking about the problems facing chimpanzees and the increasingly dying forests , i began to realize how much of africa's problems are related to the development of the former colonies .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling outside of africa , giving speeches in the u . s . , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	every single place has these terrible problems .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i'm talking about , this includes pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air we breathe constantly poison us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	clay poisoned our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water is perhaps one of the most tense issues that we have to face in this century , where water is contaminated with agriculture , industrial , homeindustrial chemicals all over the world , and those products don't seem to benefit from the past .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	the red trees are cut down and the tsunami are getting heavier .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil etching .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we're burning fossil fuels in consequences , along with something called greenhouse gases , causing climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	finally , all around the world , people are starting to believe that something is happening , that something is wrong with our climate .
全球氣候互相牽連	global weather is connected .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the disadvantages amongst others are poor people .
已經受影響的是非洲	africa has been affected .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in subsaharan africa , droughts are very serious .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	and when it finally rains up , it often leads to floods and more unfortunate adversity , poor , hunger and disease , all the time .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's a lot of people who live in land that's too poor to buy food because the land is stripped away , and therefore can't get out .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so , with desertification , it's desertification , it's delayed , and at the same time , the last tree is cut down .
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	this is not just happening all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's strange that when i travel around the world with so many young people , they seem to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we seem to have lost the wisdom of indigenous peoples .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	i want to ask the question , why is this ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some kind of disconnect between the brain and the heart of this abnormal brain technology that's shown in this abnormal brain versus compassion in a nonscientific term for love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i talk to them , basically they're emotionally low , or they're just angry , or they're suffering , they're angry , they're more or less the same thing , " we feel like it's because we feel like you've damaged our future and we can't do anything about it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we've certainly destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i think , since i've been so big , how we've damaged this beautiful earth , i feel this despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	and we started this project that we call the roots and shoots project , and it just started here , tanzania has now spread to 97 countries around the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is the basis of metaphorical meaning .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	the shoots look tiny , under sunlight , but under brick walls .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	bricks can recognize the environmental and social issues we give the earth , and that's the message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds of thousands of young people around the world can get breakthroughs , for all living things , and make the world a better place .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots , every single day , every single one of us changes the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have a choice: every single one of us in this room , we have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	very poor people don't have a choice , and we're going to change those things so that we can have a choice for the poor .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the group and the roots and shoots had three options .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	it's dependent upon membership , the country , the city , the country , the country , to choose a different alternative .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	essentially , our plan now continues to go from university to university , and as more adults start to build their own group of roots and shoots .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chooses three different ways to create a better world , to recognize that all of these different issues are interconnected with each other .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their programs will help their own human communities .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and then , if they do , they can raise money to help the communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their programs will help animals not only be wildlife , including domestic animals .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their programs will help us coexist .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message in all of these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , our families , our communities , our nations , our religious beliefs , and our relationship to the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we can't continue to destroy the world that it is .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	right here in africa , just picking one or two shoots groups that are implementing just one or two programs in tanzania , uganda , kenya , congo , brazavil , cameroon and other groups . i mean , 97 countries in the world .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they sell chickens in refugee nutrition , they sell chicken eggs , they eat very thin income , or they just give them chicken eggs to their families , and they feel pride and authority because they grow their own vegetables , and then they don't depend .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this was an example of a psychological help that was done in uganda .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	these programs implement themselves in ways that help them reshape themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	and once again , they become socially useful members .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implement that program in prison .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time to implement more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they also work on hiv and their virus .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	that's the roots and shoots program , and it's a very important component of it being talked to a lot of kids .
還有無意懷孕及類似事情年輕人更願意聽別的孩子的 , 而不是成人的	it's about unintended pregnancy and things like that , where young people are more willing to hear from other kids than adults .
希望 。 我周遊世界被問及的就是這個問題 " 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看著你的黑猩猩數量在減少 , 從世紀之交的大約一百萬到現在的不足15萬 。 那麼多其它動物也一樣	hope . the question that i have asked the world around me is this question: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you're watching your chimpanzees decrease , from about a million to about 150 , 000 of them today . so the same is true for many more animals .
森林消失 , 過去是森林的地方變成沙漠	the jungles disappeared , used to be the forests to turn into deserts .
你真的有希望 ? " 嗯 , 有 。	you're really hopeful ? " well , yes .
你不可能來參加象ted這樣的會議 , 卻不報希望 , 對吧 ?	you can't come to a conference like ted without hope , right ?
當然 , 有希望 。 希望之一是這令人稱奇的人腦	of course , there is hope . hopefully , one of these remarkable human brains .

我計劃是航行到垃圾環流帶 , 提高對於此汙染的高度重視 , 開始回收塑膠 , 切割它變成小片 , 然後冷壓變成塑膠塊 , 它可能被用來作為欠發達社群的建築材料 。	i plan to sail to the garbage stream , raise the height of the pollution and start recycling the plastic , cut it into a tiny slice , and turn it cold into a plastic chunk , which may be used as a building material for the community that it owes .
我同那些曾去過垃圾環流帶的人們談過 , 他們也曾研究過塑膠汙染對海洋環境的汙染 , 交談之後 , 我開始意識到海上清理塑膠相比起全球每天產生塑膠的生產量就如大海撈針一樣 , 我必須回過頭想想 , 要展望更大的藍圖 。	i've been talking to people who've been to the garbage stream , and they've studied the pollution of plastic pollution in the marine environment , and after talking , i've come to realize that cleaning plastic is as much as the global needle in the world , and i have to come back to thinking about the bigger blueprint of it .
真正的解決辦法就是:我們需要在源頭找到解決方法 。	the real solution is this: we need to find solutions to solutions at the source .
我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the sources of plastic in onetime source of plastic , so they won't go to the sea on a global scale .
看看這個 , 我也知道我非常生氣 。	look at this , and i know that i'm angry .

我不僅僅是關心塑膠環流帶 , 也包括超市的塑膠包圍圈 。	i'm not just caring about plastic streams , but also about supermarket plastic coils .

我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i , along with a bunch of other people , have concerned about the plastic pollution problem , built the plastic pollution coalition .

大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	people want to be able to see , especially when plastic is turning into a plastic bottle , the overwhelming majority of plastic bottles are only being recycled
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be reconstructed into a plastic bottle , or reused to be recycled , it's getting recycled and plastic bottles made into small plastic bottles that no longer be recycled into plastic bottles .
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a big problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	the other thing that we're looking at and getting people thinking is that we're going to reduce the principle of three relations , reuse , recycle , and a fourth principle , and that is that it's refusing to use .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever you're refusing to use plastic and disposable plastics .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there's alternatives . some of them are very old .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i myself am gathering these cool , thermal glass containers , using these replacements of hipsters and trachealists to store food .
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i knew i was doing it for myself and my family .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	we have chosen to use stainless steel and glass bottles that are easy , you know if you go out with a stainless steel bottle and fill it with water or filter it with water instead of buying plastic bottles .
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	and i suspect what i'd like to tell you is that i know all of you know that this plastic pollution knows a lot about this ocean of plastic as a serious problem , but it's a problem that we're all generating as consumers , and we can address it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	we taught people by raising the consciousness of this issue to choose an alternative product to solve this problem .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you choose to use an alternative product , you refuse to use a onetime sexual plastic and disposable plastic .
我們可以切斷源頭 , 阻止這塑膠汙染到我們的海洋裡 , 透過如上4r行動 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的家園 , 拯救我們自己 。	we can cut off the source and stop the plastic pollution in our oceans , and save our oceans , like 4rs , and save ourselves .

但是 , 我不認同 。	but i don't agree .
假設 , 當你在ted遇到某人 , ted , 毫無疑問 , 是每年最佳的社交場所 。 難道你會不跟人家握手 , 然後說: " 你能等一會嗎 ? 我要用手機google一下你 。 "	let's say when you meet someone at ted , ted , without a doubt , the best social place in the year . why don't you shake someone's hand , and say , " can you wait for that one ? i'm going to google you on your phone . "
或者 , 當你在超市裡 , 站在一排巨大的貨架前 , 面對著各種各樣的廁紙 , 難道你會拿出手機 , 開啟瀏覽器登入一個網站 , 嘗試去決定到底哪一種廁紙才是最環保的 , 最應該買的 ?	or when you're standing in a supermarket and you're standing in front of a giant shelf dealing with all kinds of toilets , are you going to take out your phone , and turn on your browser into a website , trying to decide which kind of toilet paper is the most ecological ?
所以說 , 我們並沒有一個便捷的渠道去獲取這些資訊 , 這些能幫助我們做出應該要幹什麼的最佳決定的資訊 。	so we don't have a quick channel to get the information that's going to help us make the best decisions we need to make .
因此 , 我的實驗室的研發團隊完成了一系列的發明 , 在不改變使用者行為的條件下 , 幫助使用者快速簡單的獲取這些資訊 。	so my lab's r&amp ; d team finished a series of inventions without changing the user's behavior and helping users rapidly pull that information out quickly .
現在 , 我將這個裝置展示給大家 。 這是我們至今最成功的版本 , 仍然在不斷改進 。	now , i'm showing this to you . this is the most successful version of our time . it's still improving .
我現在正佩戴著我們其實是把市面上常見的一些元件組裝在了一起 。 順便提一下 , 目前這個裝置的成本是350美元 。	i'm wearing now we're actually assembling some of the elements that we see on the market , and by the way , the cost of this device is 350 dollars .
我佩戴著一個相機 , 就是一個簡單的網路攝像頭 , 一個便攜的用電池供電的投影儀和一個小鏡子 。	i wear a camera , a simple webcam head , a portable battery projector and a little mirror .
這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these components communicate with my cell phone in my pocket as a communication and computation device .
畫面中 , 是我的天才學生pranavmistry , 他設計並製造了這整套系統 。	in this image , it was my genius student pranav mistry who designed and created this entire system .
我們可以看到 , 當他靠近任何表面時 , 資訊就會被投影到表面上 , 他就用雙手來進行操作 。	we can see that when he approaches any surface , the information is projected onto the surface , and he operates with both hands .
系統會跟蹤四個主要的手指 。	the system is following four major fingers .
在這裡 , 你可以看到他戴著用於標示的指套 。	here , you can see him wearing a suit used for the icon .
如果你想要更美觀 , 可以把你的指甲染成不同的顏色 。	if you want to be more beautiful , you can dye your fingernails into different colors .
攝像頭會跟蹤這四個手指 , 識別他的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以開啟longbeach的地圖 , 進行放大或者縮小等等操作 。	the camera is going to track these four fingers , identify any hand gesture , for example , and he's going to open a longng beach map to an amplify or shrink the manipulation .
這個系統也能識別 " 象徵性手勢 " , 比如 , 當你做出這個 " 拍照手勢 " , 系統就會拍照 , 把你面前的東西拍下來 。	the system also identifies symbolic gestures , such as when you make a symbolic gesture , and the system takes a picture of what's in front of you .

能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	the ink that conducts electricity , the lights turns out by transparent windows , windows that play music really exists . catari mota says it's time to try them now . mota will lead us to understand these novel and magical materials , and she says that the best way to make clear these materials is to experiment with them and try and play them over and over and over and over again .
creativity , design , technology	lots , lots of things , things that we know about .
catarinamota:玩轉智慧材料	catarina mota: play with smart materials .
我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i had a portuguese friend whose grandfather converted into a bicycle and a washing machine into a car for the family .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did this because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly , he knew how to fix a car .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	once upon a time , we knew a few principles of mechanical work and how they were made , so we could make and maintain them ourselves , or at least based on our wise purchases of understanding .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these pragmatic skills of diy were lost in the lower half of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but right now , the maker community and the opensource model is bringing this knowledge of the work of these objects back into our lives , and i believe we need to bring this knowledge to the next level , the components that make these objects .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	a lot of us know what traditional materials like paper and fabrics are made of , and how they're produced .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some amazing future composites such as transformable plastics , conductive oil paint , shifting fabrics and glowing fabrics .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's have a look at new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to abandon traditional printed circuit boards or wires methods that conduct electrical inks to draw boards .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	for example , this little device that i'm holding in my hand is a touch sensor that we use to make a touch sensor using conductive ink , and once it reaches the human skin , it lights up .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	conductive ink has been used by artists , and the latest advancements have shown that we'll soon be able to apply it to laser printers and lasers .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a sheet of paper that was bathed in color , alanine .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	immersed a paper just by a regular acrylic acid around the edges , and this is immersed with a paper that's acrylicated , and when we turn on the light , it lights up and it lights on .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	as far as we know , this material has been used in two areas of the interior design and multitouch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermodynamic paint changes color at a particular temperature .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to take this thing , i'm going to put it on a hot plate that's a little bit more temperature than the outside world , and you can see what's happening .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	besides other uses , this material is mostly made out of baby bottles , and it tells you when the bottle falls to the temperature of drinking temperature .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of what we often call " smart materials . "
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	within a few years , they will be applied to a lot of the objects and technological objects that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not yet have a science fiction flying car that promises us , but we can have walls that get rolled up with temperature , that window that gets seamlessly broken .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist from ken , and why am i talking about smart materials today ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i'm curious about how things are turning and how they can make things , and i believe that we should have a much deeper understanding of the components of our world , and now we don't know much about these hightech substances that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's also a lot of information about how to use these materials , and there's a lot less information about how they make it .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	right now , most of them are in trade secrets and patents only universities and large companies .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so more than three years ago , kirsty boyle and i launched a project called openmaterials .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we and anyone who wants to join us , share experiments , release information , encourage others to contribute to this effort , and collect resources like research papers and the documents produced by people like us .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we wanted to take this website and make it a massive , collective database to gather information about intelligent doityy materials .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how smart materials work and what are they made of ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first of all , because we can't influence what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and what we don't use is going to influence us backwards .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things we use , the clothes we we we wear , the houses we live in have profound effects on our behavior , health and quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation has always come from tinkerings .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	oftentimes , amateurs , not experts , invent and improve things like mountain vehicles , semiconductors , personal computers , even airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge with material science is its complexity and its demand for expensive instruments .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published a paper on a simpler method that conducts electric inks understood .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	jordanbunker on this experiment was a man who didn't have any chemistry chemistry , and he read this paper , and he repeated it with the material and tools that he had built in his workshop .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he took an oven , and he even made a vortex mixture on another scientist's maker's muse .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	jordan published his experimental results online , including all the unsuccessful things he tried , so that other people could learn and replicate this experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation was to take an experiment that was created in a university that was applied to the fully institutionalized laboratory and then repeat the garage in chicago with cheap materials and constructive to
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	based on the experimental results that he published , others could follow and design even simpler steps and improvements .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i want to share with you is that her project aims to highlight the performance of materials while focusing on the creativity and manufacturing skills of the maker .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	the electronic tools teach us how things work very strongly , but the constraints that they pass on in their designs affect the way we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to create a series of techniques to create very regular things that we teach to our materials , to free us from preconceptions .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorites in hannah's favorite trials .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " talking paper " ] all we see here is just a copper tape that's on the top of the piece of paper with an mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	on the basis of the research of marcelo college at mit , hannah used all kinds of materials to create a series of paper speakers , from ordinary copper to conductive fabric and ink .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	like jordan and many other makers , hannanah published her recipe and allowed anyone to do it again .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but paper is one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap , flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's hands worked and shared her discoveries with her , opened up a door , a new set of possibilities for beauty and innovation .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	what's interesting about makers is that we create passion and curiosity , and we don't fear failure .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we tend to solve problems from an unconventional perspective , and in the process , we end up finding other alternatives or better solutions .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to experiment with new materials , more researchers are willing to share their work ; more manufacturers are sharing their knowledge , and we're going to have a better chance of creating technology for all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i felt a little bit like a tednelson feeling in the early '70s , and he wrote , " you need to understand computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at that time , the computers were these big machines that only scientists were concerned about , and nobody would dream of playing one at home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i'm standing here today and saying , " you need to understand smart materials a little bit strange .
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	keep in mind that having pioneering knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the creation of the future .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	when we drive , we're sitting in a glass bubble , clicking on the door , pressing the gas door , and navigating ourselves with our eyes , even if we just see a few cars behind the wheel , but what if cars could change the data about position , speed and use the predictive model to make the safest route to every driver ? jennifer had constructed the world of a crash .
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer hayet: cars are averted or inevitable .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face it: driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but the fact that peacefully resemble peaceful security around the world , people put them on top of the plate , is inadvertently revealing a truth that we all know .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	the cause of death in car accidents , especially in the united states between 16 and 19yearolds in the united states , is that 75 percent of americans have nothing to do with drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	nobody got the right answer , but i remember when i first got in a car accident .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was a new driver , and i was driving on the freeway , and i suddenly saw the brake lights in the front of me .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , okay , he's slowed down , and i'm slowing down .
我踩了剎車	i stepped on the brakes .
但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the guy in front of me wasn't slowing down .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he parked , and he parked in the highway , and suddenly stopped .
速度從65邁瞬降到0	it drops from 65 to zero .
我猛踩剎車	i squirmed on the brakes .

貝基布蘭頓計劃在一年裡就在他的小貨車裡住並且遊歷全國 , 但是當沮喪加劇而且自由作家的工作泡湯的時候 , 他的旅營就變成了無家可歸了 。 在這個溫馨的演講中 , 她描述了她作為美國無家可歸的工作者之一的獨特經歷 。	during the year , becketon planned to live in his van and travel throughout the country , but when a depressed and freeright writer became homeless , and in this beautiful talk , she described her unique experience as homeless as an american worker .
adventure , happiness , life , personalgrowth , poverty , socialchange , society , storytelling	adventureture , happiness , lifelike plasticity , verty , the head of the group , the head of change , hasn't seen it .
貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	becky brandton: i've been homeless for a year .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , a journalist , and i'm also a strongly pleading person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned a lot about new things .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and one of the things that i learned about three years ago was to become invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my newspaper editor's job , and after my father died in february , i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	his death struck me very big .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	and it's doing this because there's a lot of things that i want to perceive and deal with .
旅遊時我天天都在露營 。 並且決定在休旅車裡住一年就當作是一段長期野營旅行 。	i was camping every single day while traveling , and i decided to live in the suv as a longterm pursuit .
所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i took my cat , my rot wilbur and camping equipment , and loaded to chevy car in 1975 , driving to the sunset , but had never imagined three serious things .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	one: societal housing even a tiny room equals human value .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i didn't realize how seriously the negative language of the others is about us if we let go of it .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i'm not aware that homelessness is a lifestyle , not a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	well , first of all , it's pretty good to be living in a car .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was showering , and i was frequently eating .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and it's time to display emotions .
但是後來 , 因我父親去世而帶來的悲憤和痛沮開始加劇 。	but the anger and the pain that my father died began to increase .
我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my freelance writer's job is over , and i need to find a fulltime job to pay my bills .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	what happens when we move from a very gentle spring to a very hot summer ?
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	it doesn't matter if the car parks anywhere is to say it's pretty obvious that i'm carrying a cat and a dog and it's very hot .
貓從車窗來回的跑 。	the cat comes back from the window of the car .
狗跑到了狗狗護理中心 。	the dog went to the dog nursing center .
不管什麼時候 , 只要可以 , 我就會去用在辦公大樓和卡車車站裡員工用的淋浴 。	anytime soon , i'm going to go to the showers that are used in office buildings and truck stops .
或者在公共衛生間裡洗洗 。	or washing it in public health .
在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	in the middle of the night , i rarely get under 80 degrees fahrenheit , which makes me almost impossible to sleep .
食物在高溫下腐壞 。	food rotates at high temperatures .
冷藏櫃裡的冰幾個小時就化完了 , 非常苦悶的時期 。	the ice in the refrigerator several hours had finished , very painful periods .
我沒錢找公寓 , 或者找不到讓我可以養狗和貓的地方 。	i didn't have any money to find apartments or to find places where i could feed my dogs and my cats .
我不想把它們拋棄 。 所以我繼續待在旅行車裡 。	i didn't want to throw them away . so i kept staying in the van .
但炎熱的天氣使我飽受折磨以至於在夜裡走50英尺到車外面的公共衛生間都懶的動 。 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。	but the hot weather made me so suffering that i could walk 50 feet out of the car and be lazy with a bucket and a garbage bag .
當冬天來臨的時候 , 溫度驟降到零度以下 。 然後就一直這麼冷 。	when winter came , the temperatures dropped below zero , and it stayed that cold .
我又遇到了一堆新問題 ,	i've had a lot of new questions .
每晚我的車都停在不同的地方 。 這樣才可以不讓警察發現以至於和警察爭吵 。	every night my cars park in different places so that they can't allow the police to realize that it's arguing with the police .
當然 , 並不是每次都成功 。	of course , not all of them were successful .
但是 , 我覺得我已無力掌控自己的生活了 。	but i felt like i had no control over my life .
我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i don't know when or how it happened , so quickly i went from being a talented writer , journalist to being a homeless woman in the vehicle , incredibly fast .
我並沒有變 。 我的智商沒有降低 。	i didn't change . my iq didn't decrease .
我的才能 , 我的正直 , 我的價值 , 所有關於我的這些東西都還是一樣 。	my talent , my integrity , my value , all of these things still remain the same .
但是從某種程度上 , 我還是改變了 ,	but in a way , i still have changed .
我越來越沮喪 , 像一個漩渦一樣不斷地往下沉 。	i was getting frustrated , like a gyre , going down and down .
後來有人介紹我去一個專為無家可歸之人開的健康診所 。	then someone introduced me to a health clinic that was specifically returned to homeless .
我去了 。 我有三天都沒有洗澡了 ,	i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .
我和其他那些排隊的人一樣沮喪 , 身上的味道也很難聞 。	i was as depressed as the rest of those lines , and the smell was terribly difficult .
我只是沒有喝醉或者興奮 。	i'm just not drunk or excited .
當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when people are homeless , they realize , including a professor who used to teach in college , they say , " you're not homeless , what's really happening here ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people don't see me as homeless , but i do think of myself .
後來 , 教授聽了我的故事後他說 , " 你有工作 , 有希望 。	later , the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job , you have hope .
真正無家可歸的人並沒有希望可言 。 "	the people who are homeless don't want to say anything . "
診所針對我沮喪開的藥物的副作用讓我有點自殺的傾向 。 我還記得當時想 , " 如果我自殺了 , 可能沒人會發現的 "	the side effects of the clinic was kind of suicidal to me , and i remember thinking , " if i commit suicide , i might not have found it . "
在那不久後 , 我的一個朋友就告訴我 , 她聽說提姆路塞特 , 一個全國知名的記者在全國播放的電視節目上談論到了我 。	not long after that , a friend of mine told me that she heard that tim russett , a nationally famous journalist , spoke about me on national tv .
一篇我寫的關於我父親的短文 , 在他去世前一年寫的 , 被收錄到了提姆的新書裡 。	an essay that i wrote about my father , written about a year before he died , was in tim's new book .
他那時在做巡迴演講 , 提到我的寫作 。	he was speaking on tour at the time , talking about my writing .
當我發現提姆路塞特 , 前meetthepress節目的調解員 , 在談論我的寫作 。 而我卻生活在停在沃爾瑪停車場裡的旅行車裡面 , 我開始笑了 ,	when i found tim ruther , the former meetpress press , talking about my writing , and i lived in a van in the walmart parking lot , i started laughing .

這對已有世界秩序行得通嗎 ?	is there any world order that works ?
我們需要一個珍重生命的世界並且每人都能夠有豐富多彩的生活而不僅僅是特權者的權力	we need a world that values life , and that is enormously colorful to everyone , not just the power of privilege .
一月份我參觀了費爾南多.波特羅的繪畫展覽在柏克利大學的圖書館中	in january i visited fernando portero's drawing exhibition in the library of berkeley .
在美國除了紐約展覽廳沒有博物館或展覽廳會展示波特羅的作品他們沒有膽量展示這些繪畫因為繪畫主題是關於阿布格萊布監獄	in addition to new york exhibition halls , there are no museums or exhibition chambers showing portero's works , and they aren't afraid to show them paintings , because the article is about
展覽有著大量的虐待和侮辱的繪畫在浩繁的波特羅風格中	the exhibition had massive abuse and paintings of insults in a vast portalo style .
我沒有辦法得到這些圖象從我的腦海中或者心中	i can't get these images out of my head or my heart .
我最害怕的是不純潔的力量	what scares me the most is the unclean power .
我害怕力量的濫用以及力量所造成的暴力	i'm afraid of the abuse of power and the violence caused by it .
在我們的種族中 , 男人們定義現實然後逼迫他人接受現實遵守規則	in our species , men define reality , and force others to accept the rules of reality .
規則常常發生變化 , 但總是對男性有益就這樣 , 在一致遵循的狀況下在經濟上並不成立的規則卻完美地存在	the rules occur more often , but they always benefit men , in the circumstances where the rules aren't economically perfect .
從上到下 , 一層層的力量濫用	from top to bottom , one layer of strength abuses .
女性和兒童 , 尤其是貧窮的 , 就這樣處於底層	women and children , especially poverty , are at the bottom .
即使是最一無所有的男人也有人被他凌虐常常是婦女或者兒童	even the most devoid of men also had someone abused by a woman or child .
我再也受不了少數人操縱多數人透過性別 , 收入 , 種族和階級的手段	i suffer from the power that a few people manipulate by gender , by income , by race and by class .
我認為現在時機已經成熟可以根本性地改變我們的文明	i think the timeline is now so mature that it will fundamentally change our civilization .
不過若要真正改變 , 就需要讓婦女的力量參與到世界當中	but in order to really change , we need to engage women's strength into the world .
我們需要讓足夠的婦女擁有權力並且培養男人心中的婦女力量	we need enough women to empower and cultivate the women in men .
這裡當然是指年輕男人了	this is of course the young man .
老男人們都沒求了 , 只能等著他們死光	old men didn't ask anymore , only to wait for them to die .
的確我也想擁有索菲亞羅蘭的長腿和著名的酥胸	and indeed i wanted to have long legs of sophia loren and famous breasts .
不過若是可以選擇 , 我寧願擁有勇敢的心像旺加里.馬塔伊 , 蘇曼麗.馬恩 , 珍妮和羅斯.馬培德那樣的	but if i could choose , i would rather be brave , like wangari maathai , sumali , sumari marn , jennie and ross mallbed .
我想讓世界變得更好	i wanted to make the world a better place .
不僅僅是消極地等待改變 , 而是參與改變	it's not just about negativity waiting to change , it's about changing .
為什麼不這樣 ? 這是能夠做得到的 。 看看這裡 , 充滿了知識 , 活力 , 才華和科技	why not ? it's possible . look at this , full of knowledge , dynamic , talent and technology .
讓我們走出冷氣房 , 捲起袖子開始行動 , 帶著我們的熱情創造一個近乎完美的世界	let's get out of the cold room , roll our sleeves into action , carry our passion , to create an almost perfect world .
在一個倫敦那麼大的城市裡 , 每天都要消耗掉三千萬噸糧食 。 但是 , 這些食物都從何而來 ? 建築師carolynsteel探討每天餵養一個城市的神話 , 介紹古代的食物運輸如何影響城市的形成和發展 。	in a city the size of london , 30 million tons of food are used every day , but where are these foods came from , carolyn steel has looked at the myth of feeding a city on a daily basis and introduced how food was transported to the city and development .
cities , culture , food , globalissues	" aren't you ? " are you going to go towards global iss ? "

如何餵養一個城市 ?	how do you feed a city ?
這是我們這個時代的一個重大問題之一 。	this is one of the major problems of our time .
然而很少人會問這個問題 。	however , very few people ask this question .
我們習以為常了 , 我們走進商店的時候走進餐廳的時候 , 或是一個小時後我們進入這個劇院的門廳總會有食物等著我們它們很神奇地從某個地方冒出來	we were so used to walking into the shop when we were walking into the restaurant , or an hour later , we'd go into this room and there'd be food , waiting for us to come out somewhere .
然而 , 當你想像每一天 , 在一個倫敦那麼大的城市 , 要生產足夠的食物運輸、交易這些食物 , 烹飪 , 食用 , 最後扔棄它們而且類似的事情每天都發生著在地球上的每一個城市都如此每個城市都有食物供應 , 這件事很不可思議	however , when you think about a day in a city the size of london that produces enough food transportation , trade these foods , cooking , eating , finally throwing it away , and things like that happen every single city on the planet every single day , food supply , it's incredible .
我們住在每天有食物供應的城市 , 彷彿這是世界上最自然的事情 , 我們忘記了我們也是動物 , 所以我們需要進食 , 事實上我們要依賴自然界就如同我們的祖先要依賴自然界一樣 。	we live in everyday cities as if it's the most natural thing in the world , and we forget that we are also animals , so we need to eat , and in fact we depend on the natural world as our ancestors depend on it .
隨著我們越來越多人到城市生活 , 越來越多的自然界正在變成我身後的這些特別的景象這是巴西matagrosso的大豆田用來種食物養活我們	as more and more of us go to cities , more and more of the natural world is becoming this peculiar scene behind me , this is the brazilian gagroso soybean field to grow our food .
這些特別的景象我們很少人親眼目睹過	these are very peculiar scenes that few of us have seen firsthand .
越來越多的這些地貌不只是生產食物養活我們	these landscapes are increasingly more than producing food to feed us .
隨著我們越來越多人移居城市越來越多人吃肉所以每年全球有三分之一的糧食現在是用來餵動物而不是餵養我們人類	as more and more of us move into cities , more and more people are eating meat , so a third of the global food every year is now feeding animals rather than feeding them .
雖然說需要3倍的糧食事實上卻是10倍的食物來餵養一個人 , 如果從餵養動物的糧食也計算在內這並不是一個很有效率的餵養方式	even though it takes three times more food , it's actually 10 times as much food to feed one person , and if it's food feeding them , it's not a very efficient way of feeding them .
這是一個越來越重要的問題	this is an increasingly important question .
到2050年 , 預測有兩倍的人口將在城市居住	by 2050 , it's predicted that twice as many people will live in cities .
預測到也將需要兩倍的肉和奶類製品的消耗	it predicts that it will also cost twice as much meat and dairy as it is .
所以肉的消耗和城市化是共同發展的	so meat consumption and urbanization are coevolving .
這就將引發一個很重大的問題	and that leads to a major problem .
要餵養60億的飢餓人口在2050年	six billion hunger people are fed by 2050 .
這是個大問題.如果我們還像我們現在這麼發展 , 我們很可能沒法在2050年解決這個問題	it's a big problem . if we're still here , we probably won't solve this problem by 2050 .
每年有1900萬公頃的雨林消失它們用作開墾新的耕地	190 million hectares of rainforest disappear every year , and they colonize new agricultural fields .
儘管與此同時我們也失去等量的現有耕地 , 因為鹽鹼化或水土流失	but at the same time , we're losing an equal amount of existing arable residence because of salinization or water loss .
我們也急需化石燃料	we desperately need fossil fuels .
在歐洲 , 我們需要10卡路里的能量來生產1卡路里為我們消耗的食物	in europe , we need 10 calories to produce one calories for the food that we consume .
儘管這些食物我們都是花了很多功夫才生產出來事實上我們卻不珍惜它們	and despite all of this food , it took a lot of work to produce it , but we didn't really value it .
在美國有一半食物被扔棄	half of the food in the u . s . is thrown away .
最終 , 在這漫長過程的最後我們將沒法養活我們這個地球	ultimately , at the end of this long process , we will not be able to feed our planet .
我們中10億人肥胖 , 還有多於10億的人處於飢餓中	one billion of us are obese , and more than one billion are hungry .
這些都沒有道理	none of this makes any sense .
當你發現現在80%的全球食物貿易僅由五家跨國公司控制 , 這是挺可怕的	when you find out that 80 percent of the global food trade is controlled by just five multinational companies , it's terrifying .
隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界正在接受西方的飲食	as we move into cities , the world is accepting western diet .
如果我們展望未來這不是個可持續的飲食方式	if we look to the future , it's not a sustainable diet .

更重要的是 , 我們應該怎麼做 ?	and more importantly , what should we do ?
先回答那個較簡單的問題 , 首先我想說 , 在大概1萬年前是這個過程的開始在古代的中東地區也就是廣大的新月狀的地區	and i want to start by saying that it's a simpler question , first of all , about 10 , 000 years ago , that process started in ancient middle east which is a vast area of the new moon .
因為你可以看到它是新月形的	because you can see that it's the moon .
同時它也是廣大的	it's also vast .

這並不是偶然因為農業和城市是緊密聯絡的.它們需要彼此	this is not an accident , because agriculture and cities are intimately connected . they need each other .
因為糧食的發現我們的遠古祖先 , 第一次第一次生產出足夠的糧食並且產量穩地 , 這幫助他們長期居住下來	and because of the discovery of food , our distant ancestors , for the first time , will produce enough food and produce enough production for a long time .
如果我們看一下當時那些居住地我們可以看到他們是緊密的	if we look at those settlements where we lived , we see that they were close .
他們被農田圍繞並由一些大的廟宇統領著例如這一個在烏爾的神殿事實上 , 他們是很有效的精神統領 , 食物分發中心 , 兩者結合	they are led by temples surrounded by farms and dominated by large temples , such as this one in ur , the temples , and in fact , they're very effective mental reigns , food distribution centers .

這樣是在古代能實現的唯一的方法因為陸上運輸相當困難鑑於路況不好	this is the only way that ancient peoples can do it , because it's very difficult to transport on the continents , because the roads are bad .

所以羅馬常常發動戰爭攻打像迦太基和埃及那樣的國家僅僅是為了得到他們的糧食儲備	so rome constantly wages war and attacks countries like ghama and egypt just to get their food reserves .
其實 , 事實上 , 你可以把帝國的擴張理解為一種長期的軍事化的購物狂歡	in fact , you could popularize the empire's sprawl as a longterm military shopping master .
事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 。 我不得不指出的是羅馬在一個時期 。 我認為這非常特別	in fact , what i love about this is that rome was in a period of time . i think that's quite extraordinary .

但是還有一件有趣的事情發生在前工業化的世界	but there's another interesting thing that's happening in the preindustrialized world .
如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖我們可以看見作物從泰晤士河畔出產的位於地圖的底部	if we were to look at maps of london in the 17th century , we could see crops being produced from the base of the thames .

肉是一個非常不同的故事了因為 , 動物自己走向城市	meat is a very different story , because animals themselves are moving to cities .

然後當它們在東部降落的時候具體說來是在戚普塞街 , 也就是它們被賣掉的地方這也就是戚普塞街被稱為 " 家禽 " 街的原因	and when they land in the east , specifically on mutanpse street , which is what they sold , and that is why they called mrsey street .

因為街道和公共區域是食物買賣的唯一地點	because streets and public regions are the only place where food purchases are sold .

事實上 , 當你在星期日吃午飯的時候你將很有可能聽到窗外的牛羊的叫聲在三年以前	in fact , when you're at lunch on sunday , you're very likely to hear from a sheep outside the window . three years ago .
因此 , 顯然他是一個有機城市屬於有機迴圈中的一個部分	so , apparently , he's a part of an organic city that belongs to an organic loop .
但是 , 10年後 , 一切都改變了	but then 10 years later , everything changed .
這是大西鐵路在1840的照片	this is a picture of the west railway in 1840 .
你可以看見 , 一些早期的鐵路乘客們是豬和羊群	as you can see , some of the earlier passengers were pigs and sheep .
一夕之間 , 這些動物不再走進市場	all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into the market .
他們被屠宰了在鄉村的某個地方	they were slaughtered somewhere in the countryside .
然後他們透過鐵路來到了城市	and they came to the city through the railway .
這些改變了一切	these things have changed everything .
首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first of all , he's the first time that the city has grown , possibly , what scale and shape .
城市發展過去受到地理的限制城市需要透過很艱難的方式獲得食物	cities were developed to be constrained by geography , and cities needed to get food in difficult ways .
突然 , 他們從地理限制中解放了出來	suddenly , they emancipated from geography .
你可以看看倫敦的地圖在鐵路建成後的90年它從容易餵飽的一小點透過動物步行到市場等方式成長成為大型的奢侈的大都市步行運輸再也不能餵飽每個人不論是對人還是對動物	you can look at a map of london 90 years after the railroad built , it grew from a very easy feeding dot through animal walks to markets and so forth as luxury urban urban skills , and then you couldn't feed anybody , whether it's for humans or for animals .
當然 , 這僅僅是開始 。 當汽車代替了火車這真正標誌這個過程的結束	of course , this is only the beginning . when cars displaced the train , the real symbol was the end of the process .
這是城市的最終解放從自然的束縛中完全的解放了	this is the final emancipation of the city , liberating from its natural restraint .
這樣型別的城市沒有了原來城市的味道亂糟糟的市容 , 當然也缺少了人因為沒有人想要在這麼大的一塊地方步行	it doesn't have any original , messy , town , metropolitan smells , and , of course , missing people , because nobody wants to be walking in such a big place .
事實上 , 他們都開小汽車去購買食物了開車去郊外的超級市場買回來一週需要的食物然後考慮到底如何規劃這些食品	in fact , they drive small cars to buy food , to drive to the supermarket to the suburbs , buy food that's required for a week , and then think about how to plan these foods .
這時刻 , 食物和城市的關係 , 完全的改變了	this is the moment when the relationship between the food and the city changed completely .
過去買食物是在市中心在城市的最核心地帶	food used to be the most core place in the city .
買賣食物曾經是一種社會性的活動 ,	buying food used to be a social event .

mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	instead of the idea of a selfassembly projection by the mit researcher kazbe , we can create our own materials that are like dna chains , and we're still bagging them at the earliest stages of a big idea ; tizzi shows us three projects that are still undergoing this experiment , and we can peer into the future of selfassembly .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	sk: can we make our own thing ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	today i want to show you the way in which we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe soon our buildings and machines will selfassemble , selfreplication and selfrepair .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think is the manufacturing industry , and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we have two and a half years of skyscrapers , half a million to a million , very complicated , using new technologies on steel , concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have an exciting machine that can take us into space five years , 2 . 5 million parts of it .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if you look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that can fold in naseconds , and we can reconnect with three billion base pairs of dna in about an hour .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	this is the complexity of our natural systems , but they are very efficient , much more efficient than anything we can build , much more complicated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're even more efficient in terms of energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they make few mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can selfretain longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	there's something really interesting about the natural system .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can convert it to our built environment , then there's a lot of potential in the way we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key to that is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to use our selfassembly in our bodies , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decipher the complexity of what we're building , which is our buildings and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode them into simple sequences that are basically the dna of how our buildings work .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need programming parts that will take this sequence and fold it , fold it , or remode it .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to launch , so we can code the way we want to .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some error correlated redundancy that will ensure that we're successful building is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some projects that my colleagues and i are working on to achieve this selfassembly future .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects were macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these are projects that scale up to reconstruct the robots 8 feet , 12 feet long protein .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded in machine electrical devices , sensors .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you need to decode the way you want to fold into a series of angles: minus 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , that sort of thing ; a series of angles , or turn around , that can transmit the sequence by wire .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit captures its message such as negative 120 and rotates , checks if it rotates to its position and then sent sequences to its neighbors .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there are some brilliant scientists , engineers , designers working on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think this project really reveals: is this really scalable ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it costs thousands of dollars to build this eightfoot robot .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we really expand it ? can we actually embed the robot in every single part ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next problem is looking passively , or passively trying to make recombinations programmable .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it went a step further , and it tried to do actual computing .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	basically embedded in the infrastructure of most computations , the digital logic gate , directly into the parts .
這是與非門 。	this is the opposite .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each of these has a calculated doors with two input 4 .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one is the input from the user , like you're building bricks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other one was the input from the previous brick .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it exports into three dimensions .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	it means that users build bricks in the way they want to .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it calculates according to the kinds of instructions you made earli
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	now it starts to move or fall in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	if you look on the left , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , down .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , 0] input is 1 output , which is up .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so what this really means is that our structure now contains the blueprints that we want to construct .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so the information about building something is already embedded in it .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	it means that we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	this is what i call selfdirected replication , because you have the exact blueprints in your structure .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if you have errors , you can change parts .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	all of the local information is embedded in there , showing you how to fix it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that climbs , reads it and outputs one by one .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's embedded directly ; there's no external input .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the last project i'm going to show is called bias , and it's probably the most exciting example we're seeing in the passive selfassembly system .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it has reconstructiveness and programmability that makes it available for a completely passive system .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	it's basically a series of elements that you have .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is completely identical , and they are biased .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	each link , or each element wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you want to assemble chains , you have to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	to tell each unit whether it's left or right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	when you shake the chain , it origamis the structure that you code for it , so in this case , a spiral , fire , two connected cubes .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	you're basically programming in 3d or onedimensional , twodimensional strands that are completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what is the future that preprograms us ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	i think what this tells us is the possibility that these selfassembles and machines are selfreplicating , selfrepairing and selfrepair .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	there's new programmability in these parts .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	you get new possibilities for computing .
我們將有空間計算 。	we're going to have spatial computing .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines all perform physical computations .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	what an amazing parallel computation and distributed computing and new possibilities .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's an exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	and i think these projects that i've shown you are just a step towards the future , if we're making these new technologies for a new selfassembly world .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've stepped onto the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even gone down to the bottom twice . what's worth exploring for our children , biologists and nathan wolf come up with the answer: almost everything . 最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	i recently was in beloit , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i was there to commemorate a 20thcentury explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	when he was at the museum of natural history , andrews led a series of expeditions to the unknown , like here in gobid beach .
他是個了不起的人物 。	he was an amazing figure .
他後來據說是印第安娜瓊斯角色的原型 。	he later said it was the prototype of the indiana jones character .
當我在威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市的時候 , 我給一群中學學生上了一堂公開課 。	when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i took a public class for a group of middle school students .
我現在想告訴你們 , 如果真的有什麼比在ted做演講還難的話 , 那就是嘗試保持他們的注意力一群上千個12歲的孩子 , 並保持45分鐘 。	and i want to tell you now that if it's really harder than giving a talk at ted , it's trying to keep the attention of a thousand 12yearolds and keep it for 45 minutes .

有個小女孩站起來 , 問了一個問題: " 我們該去哪裡探索呢 ? "	a little girl stood up and asked a question: " where should we explore ? "
我想我們中的絕大多數有種觀念 , 那就是 , 地球上的大探索時代已經結束 , 我們的下一代人應該去外太空或者海洋最深處從而去尋找值得探索的東西 。	i think the vast majority of our concepts are that the age of exploration on earth is over , that our next generation should go to space or the deepest of our oceans to find things that are worth exploring .
但真的是這樣嗎 ?	but is that really true ?
真的沒有重要的地方留給我們探索了嗎 ? 整個地球上都沒有 ?	is there really no important place left for us to explore ? there isn't a whole earth ?
這讓我回憶起我最喜歡的生物領域的探險家之一 。	this reminds me of one of my favorite biological adventures .
他是位未知世界的探索家 , 馬丁努斯•威廉•拜耶林克 。	he's a explorer of the unknown world , martin norse william william william billynk .
拜葉林克當初想找出引起菸草花葉病的原因 。	ballet link was originally trying to identify the cause of tobacco leaf disease .
他提取了受過感染的菸草汁液 , 然後讓這些汁液經過一層比一層更細的過濾 。	he took the infected tobacco sap and he let the sap go through a thicker filter that filters even more than one layer .
他得出一個結論 , 剩下的裡面一定有什麼東西它們比那時最小的已知的生命形態--細菌 , 還要小 。	he came to the conclusion that there was something left that was smaller than what was known as the smallest lifestyle bacteria , smaller .
他給這個神秘的東西起了個名字	he gave this mysterious thing a name .
叫它們 , 病毒在拉丁文裡是 " 毒藥 " 的意思 。	call them the viruses in latin for " poison . "
在發現病毒之後 , 拜耶林克為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。	after the discovery of the virus , byyye link opened a whole new world for us .
我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make the vast majority of the genetic information on our planet more than the sum of all other life .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and apparently there have been countless applications for viruses in the world like the eradication of smallpox , the cervical cancer vaccine that we now know is mostly caused by mammal viruses .
而且拜耶林克的發現可不是500年前的事情 。	and what brilliant found was not 500 years ago .
拜耶林克發現病毒這件事也就發生於100多年前 。	this virus happened more than 100 years ago by jellek .
也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	that means that when cars are present , we don't even know that this is the creature that makes most of our genetic information on our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some remarkable tools to help us explore the unknown world , like the depth of the genome that allow us to not just stay on the surface to look at the independent genome from a particular species , but to study the entire genome of the entire genome that our bodies and our surrounding microbial colonies , and record from that information .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these technologies to study everything from soil to skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my own institutions , we now do this all the time to find out why those rapes are so unknown to us .
稍微給你們講下這是怎麼做的 , 想象下從你們每個人那裡取一個鼻腔分泌物標本	and just to give you a hint of how it works , imagine taking a nasal secret library from each of you .
像這種事是我們經常做的 , 為了尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像流行性感冒病毒 。	things like this are something that we often do to find a respiratory virus , like a flu epidemic .
我們首先看到的是海量的遺傳資訊 。	the first thing we saw was massive amounts of genetic information .
如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start looking at the genetic information , we see conventional information of course a lot of human genetic information , but also a lot of bacteria and viruses , mostly things that are completely harmless within your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we also see some very , very surprising things .
當我們開始研究這些資訊 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊跟我們所見過的東西--任何植物 , 動物 , 真菌或者細菌 , 都對不上號 。	when we started looking at this information , we found that 20 percent of the genetic information that you see in your nose any plant , any plant , any fungus or bacteria are not numbered at all .
我們基本上對這些一無所知 。	we essentially don't know anything about these .
我們這裡的一小部分研究這些資料的人們 , 稱呼這些資訊為生物暗物質 。	a small number of people here who studied this data call this information biological dark matter .
我們知道以前從未見過這些生物暗物質 ; 這似乎可以被稱之為我們自己遺傳資訊裡的未知大陸 。	we know that these biological dark matters have never seen them before ; they seem to be called the unknown continents of our own inherited information .
而且數量非常之多 。	and there's a lot of them .
如果你認為你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊有很多生物暗物質 , 那當我們看你內臟的時候 , 那有將近40%到50%的生物暗物質 。	if you think that 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose has a lot of biological dark matter , when we look at your gut , it's close to 40 to 50 percent of the biological dark matter .
即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in the relatively sterile bloodstream , one to two percent of the information is dark matter can't be categorized , can't be judged , can't be judged , can't be categorized , can't be judged .
開始我們以為這是人為的東西 。	to start with what we thought was a manmade thing .
這些基因深度測序工具相當比較新 。	these gene sequencing tools are relatively new .
但當它們變得越來越來精確 , 我們認為這些資訊是一種新的生命 , 或者至少某一部分是種生命 。	but as they become more and more accurate , we think that information is a new form of life , or at least a part of it is a form of life .
即使這些關於解釋生物暗物質的存在的假設還處於嬰兒期 , 一個讓人非常非常激動的可能性存在著:那就是藏在這個生命裡面 , 在這些遺傳資訊裡 , 有一種沒有被識別的生命的標識 。	even these hypotheses about the presence of biological dark matter are still infancy , a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that there's a marker of life that has not been identified .
當我們探索這些一串串a/t/c/g嘌呤的時候 , 我們也許會發現全新的生命 , 就像拜耶林克 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學特性的理解 。	when we explore these strings of a/c/g purine xrex , we may find new life , like bayerink , fundamentally changing our understanding of biology .
這也許會讓我識別出困擾我們的某種癌症的原因 , 或者識別出我們不熟悉的疾病暴發的根源 , 或者創造出一種分子生物學的新工具 。	this may help me identify the cause of some form of cancer , or identify the root cause of an unfamiliar disease violence , or create a new tool in molecular biology .
我很高興的宣佈 , 和我的斯坦福、加州理工和舊金山加利福尼亞大學的同事們一起 , 我們正在開始開始一個新的行動去探索生物暗物質來尋找新生命的存在 。	i'm pleased to announce that together with my colleagues at stanford and caltech and the university of california , we're starting a new action to explore the existence of biological dark matter to seek out new life .
100多年前 , 人們還不知道病毒的存在 , 這些包含我們星球上大部分遺傳資訊的生命形態 。	more than 100 years ago , people didn't even know the presence of the virus , and these shapes contained most of the genetic information on our planet .
一百年以後 , 人類可能為我們以前完全不瞭解的新的生命形態而感到驚訝而它們就在我們眼皮底下 。	a hundred years later , humans may surprise us as surprisingly to a new form of life that we've never seen before , and they're beneath our eyes .

拜耶林克和像他一樣的人們給下一代探索者上了重要的一課----給那些像那個在伯洛伊特市的女孩一樣的人們 。	bayer link , like him , gave the next generation of explorers an important lesson for those of us in the city of belonging .

在不管你選擇的任何領域裡去探索那些暗物質吧 。	explore those dark matter in any area that you choose .
未知的事物在我們身邊無處不在它們只是在等待人類的探索 。	the unknown things are everywhere around us they're just waiting for human exploration .

那麼太陽系--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--是如何獲取這樣一個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係的呢 ?	so the solar system our environment , in our form is how do we get a special relationship with the rest of the universe ?
stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	one of the correct aspects of the stephen hawking view i mean , that's true , but it's true , but one of the things that's right is that it doesn't depend on any special physics . there's no special physics , there's no miracles happening .
其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理需要計算 , 計算需要電腦--現有的知識下不可能不需要物質來製造電腦 。	one of them is matter , because knowledge grows as a form of information processing that requires computing and computational processing and computing requires that computers currently can't be materialized to make computers .

我們的環境中充滿了證據 。	our environment is full of evidence .

而在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件存在的可能性極端之小 。	and in intergalactic space , these three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are extremely unlikely .

但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某事是物理定律所允許的 , 那麼在我們知道如何運作的情況下 , 什麼會妨礙我們去實踐它呢 ?	but the question is , in a comprehensible universe , if something's allowed by the laws of physics , then what could impede us to practice it if we know how to work ?

同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	and if we can do that , then we'll automatically feed our energy supply , because this change is going to be a nuclear reactor there evidence ?

在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can do astrophysics study to understand the laws of physics .
