但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you richard , i'm sorry , richard but i never really liked biological field trips , and i think we can do it every million years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so , in fact , intergalactic space does not have a prerequisite for the openended creation of knowledge , and any cube like this can become a center of the sameness in the universe if the knowledge of this project exists .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not the only place to be passionate about .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended set of explanations , then pretty much every other environment is ok . the earth is contaminated .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factors , here and there , are not resources , because they're enormous , but knowledge , which is scarce .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	this cosmic knowledgebased view may well , i think we feel very special , but it also gives us a sense of our own vulnerability , because it means that without the specific knowledge that we need to address our origins to our universe constantly , we will be unable to survive .
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	just a few lightyears away , a supernova explosion , we'll all be dead .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability with everything , from astrophysics to scientific experiments , and most importantly , terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he thought civilization had a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	i think he's going to talk about that in the conference later on .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think that's a good idea to describe probabilities .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him that we can survive , that we may not survive .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on probability , it's whether we can create relevant knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	the danger is certainly not unprecedented . species have been extinct .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations end . the vast majority of species and civilizations ever live in history .
如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來看我們唯一的希望是利用將我們這個種群和文明與其他物種區別開的這個特徵 , 與其他一切都區別開的這個特徵 。 也就是 , 我們與物理定律得特殊關係 。 我們創造新的解釋和知識的能力--成為存在的中心 。	if we want to be the exception , logically , our only hope is to take this feature that distinguishes our species and civilization from all other species , and that is , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations and knowledge to be the center of existence .
讓我將此運用到當前的一個論戰中 , 不是因為我想提議任何特定的解決方法 , 而只是用來闡明我所要講述的一些事 。	let me apply this to the current controversy , not because i want to propose any particular solution , but just to illustrate some of the things that i'm talking about .
這個論戰就是全球暖化 。	the controversy is global warming .
我是一個物理學家 , 但我並不是此領域的物理學家 。 就全球暖化來說 , 我只是個門外漢 。 對一個門外漢來說理智的做法是嚴肅對待權威的科學理論 。 而根據這一理論 , 已經太晚了 , 災難在所難免 。	i'm a physicist , but i'm not a physicist in this field , and i'm just a physicist in global warming , and to a global warming , reasonable practice is to take the scientific theory of authority , and according to that theory , disaster has been too late .
因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放的話 , 例如透過東京議定書之類的 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費千億美元等巨大的代價 , 那麼不管如何衡量 , 這就已經是一個災難了 。	because if our best options at the moment are to prevent carbon dioxide emissions , like the book of the tokyo protocol , for example , restrict economic activity and the cost of hundreds of billions of dollars , then this is already a disaster .
倡議的行動甚至都不是為解決問題 , 而只是稍微推遲災難的到來 。 因此災難在所難免 , 一切都已晚 , 或在所有人意識到這個危險之前就已經太晚了 。	the actions initiatives aren't even about solving problems , but they're just about postpopulation , so the disaster is inevitable , it's already too late , or it's already too late for everyone to realize this danger .
上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it's probably already too late in the 1970s , and the state of science at the time was telling us that industrial emissions would lead to a new ice age , billions of people would die .
這一教訓對我來說清晰可見 , 我不明白為什麼它沒有傳達至公眾辯論 。	this lesson to me was clearly visible , and i didn't understand why it didn't convey to public debate .
事實是我們不可能永遠知道 。 當我們知道有一個災難將要降臨 , 應對這個災難的成本要比災難本身小 , 那麼就真的沒有什麼好爭論的 。	the fact that we can't always know , that when we know that there's a disaster that's going to fall , the cost of this disaster is smaller than the cost of the disaster , then there's really no argument .
但是沒有任何預防措施 , 或者預防原則可以幫助我們避免我們還沒有預測到的問題 。	but there is no precautionary principle , or prevention principle that can help us avoid problems that we haven't predicted yet .
因此我們需要準備好去解決問題 , 而不僅僅是避免問題 。	so we need to be prepared to fix this problem , not just avoid it .
一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解決 , 這是事實 , 但是這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下 。	it's true that an ounce of prevention equals an ounce of resolution , but it's just in cases where we know what to prevent .
如果你的鼻子被打了一拳 , 醫學不會教你如何閃躲拳頭 。	if you have a punch on your nose , medicine doesn't teach you how to hide your fists .
如果醫學不再研究治病的方法 , 而是僅僅研究預防 , 那麼它將幾乎一事無成 。	if medicine stopped studying how to cure it , it was simply studying prevention , then it would be nearly nothing .
目前整個世界都在不計成本地忙著計劃來促成氣體排放量的減少 。	the whole world is planning it at no cost to facilitate a decrease in gas emissions .
而它應該趕緊計劃如何降低溫度 , 以及計劃如何在溫度升高之後如何生存 。 不是不計成本 , 而是有效地、廉價的計劃 。 而這樣的一些計劃已經存在了 , 比如在太空中放置大批鏡子來將太陽光反射出去 , 以及刺激海洋生物消費更多的二氧化碳 。	and it should hurry up on how to lower the temperature and how to survive when it gets warmer , not in cost , but inefficiently , cheaply planned , and these programs have already existed , such as responding to large mirrors in space to reflect the sunlight and encourage more carbon dioxide to the ocean .
而目前 , 這些都只是邊緣研究 。	and so far , these are just marginalized research .
人類在應對這個問題或者廣義上來說這些問題的時候 , 它們起不到核心作用 。	when humans address this question in terms of magnitude or in general , they don't have a central role .
對於我們並未知覺的問題 , 糾錯的能力--不是無限期的躲過期發生的絕對好運--是我們唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是為解決問題 , 而是為生存 。	for problems we don't perceive , the ability to be wrong isn't the absolute good luck of occurring indefinitely the only hope we have , not just for solving problems , but for survival .
我們應該拿起兩塊石碑 , 在上邊刻上銘文 。	we should take two stones and carve them on top .
其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 " 。	carved in one piece , " the problem is soluble . "
另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 " 。	carved in the other patch is , " the problem is inevitable . "
被困在不健全的制度下 , 一個國家怎麼可能脫貧呢 ? 經濟學家paulromer提出全新見解: " 特別市 " , 由多國聯合政府管理的、城市規模的管理區域 。	being trapped under a robust institution , how could a nation get out of poverty , and the economist paul romer proposed this new insight: " special markets , " by multinational government management , urbanscale .
business , culture , economics , globalissues , politics	" remission , " " hello , global issue , " he who is global . "
paulromer的全新見解:特別市	paul romer's whole new insight: the special city .
請看這張圖片 。	so here's a picture of it .
它帶給我們一個極具吸引力的謎 。	it gives us an incredibly attractive mystery .
這些非洲學生在做功課在首都機場的街燈下因為他們家裡沒有電 。	these african students are doing homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have electricity at home .
我還沒見過這幾個學生本人但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。	i haven't met these individual students , but i have met students like them .
拿那個穿綠襯衫的學生做例子 ,	take the example of the student in a green shirt .
假設他的名字叫做nelson 。	suppose his name is nelson .
我猜他肯定有個手機	i guess he's got a cell phone .
有趣的是 ,	here's the funny thing .
為什麼nelson有機會享用像手機這樣的前沿科技成果但卻不能在家用上電力 ? 人們早在100年前就已經發明瞭這一科技啊 ?	why is it that nelson has had the opportunity to enjoy advanced technological results such as mobile devices , but can't use electricity at home ? people have been developing this technology 100 years ago ?
答案是 " 制度 " 。	the answer is institutions .
不健全的制度會妨礙這種雙贏節決辦法的產生人們在一定的制度之下就不會將科技帶給像nelson這樣的人	the robust institutions prevent this kind of winning decision from generating people without any kind of institutions to bring technology to people like nelson .
什麼樣的制度呢 ?	what kind of systems ?
這個國家的電力公司需要遵守一條制度這個制度要求它在政府補貼的條件下從使用者收取極其低價電費事實上 , 電費便宜到另電力公司虧損的地步	the electricity company in this country needs to follow an institution that demands a minimum price in terms of government subsidize prices , and in fact , the electricity costs are cheap enough to reach another company loss .
所以 , 電力公司既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去給使用者接通電源	so there's no resources , no motivation for the user .
總統想要改變這個局面	the president wanted to change that .
他已經覺察到更換體制是具可能性的 。 能讓商家盈利的體制才能使有動機爭取更多使用者	he's already aware of the possibility of replacing the systems that make business profitable so that we can motivate more users .
賣nelson的手機的那個廠家也正式在制度下經營著	the manufacturer who sold nelson's cell phone was running under the institutions .
總統已經領會到制度執行良好	the president has led to a good institutional implementation .
所以他嘗試著改變現行的電價制度但來自商人以及消費者的反對的聲音四起他們想保留現行的補貼電費制度	so he's trying to change the price system , but the merchants and the consumer's voices are everywhere , and they're trying to preserve the existing subsidies .
總統無能為力 , 只能任由現行制度阻止雙贏局面產生 , 任由它妨礙改善國家	the president can't do anything about it , only works on the current institutions to stop the winwin situation from improving the country .
因此 , nelson也只能在街燈下學習	so nelson also learns in the streetlights .
真正具有挑戰性的是嘗試尋找改變制度的辦法	what's really challenging is trying to find ways to change rules .
我們可不可以發展 " 改變制度 " 的制度呢 ?	can we develop systems that change rules ?
我想說 , 我們可以把抽象化為實際或者說 , 如果我們給予人民更多選擇給予領導者更多選擇 , 領導者在很多國家也是人民麼	i mean , we can take abstraction as a reality , or if we give people more choices to leaders more choices , leaders are people in many countries as well .
但 , 兩者間的對立還是有必要解釋的	but polarity is necessary to explain it .
因為你想給予領袖的自由是像那種你給予總統提高電價一樣的自由剝奪人民在這個經濟體系中的需求自由	because freedom you want to offer to leaders is something that you offer to offer the president to freely deprive people of the economic system .
希望可以繼續享用補貼電價的自由	i hope i will enjoy the freedom of a subsidized price .
所以如果你只選取一方 , 或另一方你將面臨矛盾或摩擦	so if you just choose one side or the other , you're going to face conflict or friction .
但如果我們相辦法同時給兩者自由那麼就會產生能使我們擺脫困境的制度	but if we give both of them freedom at the same time , it creates an institution that allows us to get out of this dilemma .
nelson現在還可以享用網際網路	nelson now enjoys the internet .
他說如果你想看到制度的破壞性制度怎樣陷人民於黑暗中看一看美國家宇航局拍攝的地球夜景	he says that if you want to see the destructive institutions , the destructive institutions , the people look in the dark and look at the earth night landscape

你不會驚訝北朝鮮的制度將人民陷於黑暗	you're not surprised to the north korean institutions plunging people into darkness .
重要的是要承認南北朝鮮曾有一模一樣的制度不論法律上還是政策上而且在深層理解上準則 , 文化 , 價值 , 信仰	it's important to recognize that north korea had the same institutions , both the laws and the policies , the culture , the values , the religions .
南北分隔時 , 南北朝鮮做出了引領它們走向不同道路的選擇由不同的制度而產生	as north korea made north korea during the north , the north korean choices occurred from different roads .
因而我們可以改變 , 我們 , 人類 , 可以改變制度人際交往與相處的制度使之變得更好 , 或更壞	so we can change , we , human beings , can change institutions , interfaces , and make them better , or worse .
現在來看看另外一個地區 , 加勒比海域	let's look at another area , the caribbean water .
放大海地在這兒	zoom in to haiti .
海地也在黑暗中和鄰國多明尼加共和國相比同樣的人口總數	haiti is also in the dark compared to the neighboring country of dominican republic .
但這兩個國家和波多黎各比 , 也處於黑暗中波多黎各人口總數大概是海地或多米尼亞共和國的一半左右	but these two countries , compared to puerto rico , are also in darkness , the total population of probably haiti or tommia .
海地提醒了我們體制可因薄弱的政府而不健全	haiti reminded us that institutions are not healthy due to weak governments .
而不完全是因為政府太強制 , 比如北朝鮮	it's not entirely because governments are too mandatory , like north korea .
因此如果我們想要建立良好政策的環境我們不能總是破壞	so if we want to create environments of good policy , we can't always destroy them .

看 , 中國強烈地展示了體制改革帶來的潛力和挑戰	look , china strongly demonstrates the potential and the challenges that institutional reforms bring .

例如鋼鐵 , 印刷 , 火藥	for example , iron , printing , gunpowder .

所以在其它國家創新時 , 在發展新科技和新制度的層面上時中國已經與這些進步脫離了腳步	so in other countries , in terms of the development of new technologies and the new institutions , china has been escaped from these advances .

中國最明亮的地域你可以在輪廓的邊際看到是香港	china's brightest region , you can see on the outline , hong kong .
香港其實是中國很小的一塊地方在二十世紀的絕大部分時期都在非常不同的體制下治理著與大陸其它地方都不同體制是從當時有效的市場經濟複製出來的並由英國治理	hong kong is actually a very small place in china , and in the vast majority of the 20th century , it governs very different institutions than on the continent , in other parts of the continent where effective market economies were replicated and dominated by britain .
於19世紀五十年代 , 香港是百萬大陸人去找像縫紉 , 製作玩具之類工作的地方	in the 1950s , hong kong was a million continents to go looking for places like sewing and making toys and so forth .
但要想提高收入提高技術促進飛速增長	but to raise the income rate , skills facilitate growth .

但鄧小平本能地理解給予人民自由的重要性	but deng xiaoping understands instinctively the importance of giving freedom to its people .
所以鄧不是一下子放手讓中國立即走向市場經濟他先設立了特別行政區這樣就可以模仿英國提供可以執行市場經濟的機會向那些想要這個機會的人們	so deng xiaoping isn't about letting china get to the market economy , he's setting up this specially administrative district so that you can mimic britain's opportunity to implement the market e

這些的成功引起共識帶領整個經濟體制走向市場經濟	these successes are what led to a consensus that leads the entire economy to the market economy .
現在中國的這些例子證明以下幾點:	now , these chinese examples have shown the following points .
一:留給人民自由	one: freedom to the people .
二:在恰當的規模下操作	two: operate at the right scale .
如果你想在一個村莊改變體制 , 可以 , 但一個村的規模太小了不能帶給你如同讓百萬人一樣的效應在優質體制的治理下	if you want to change the institution in a village , it's okay , but a village is too small to give you the same kind of effect , like a million people , under the governance of a good system .
另一方面 , 一下子改變全國的體制又太大了	on the other hand , it's just too big to change the nationwide system .
如果你想改變國家體制有一部分人必然得不到照顧他們也沒有機會去評估新政的優劣給人民一個聚焦未來 , 嘗試新體制的機會	if you want to change the national institutions , some of them aren't going to get the care , and they don't have the opportunity to evaluate the disadvantage of their citizens , to try new systems .
但像城市就能給你這些機會來建立新領域開拓新體制 , 人們可以選擇	but just like cities are giving you opportunities to build new frontiers , new institutions , people can choose .
並且足夠大大到我們能得到應有的當百萬人在新體制治理下應有的效應	and it's big enough that we can get the effects of millions of people under the new rules .
所以我提議我們設想一種叫做 " 特別市 " 的東西	so i propose that we think of something called the " special city . "
首先綱領詳細說明所有的條例規則來吸引那些建設特別市的人才	first of all , the syllabus then suggests that all rules are used to attract people who are building the extraordinary .
我們需要吸引投資商他們會建設基礎設施能源系統 , 公路 , 碼頭 , 機場 , 樓房	we need to attract investors , and they build infrastructure , infrastructure , roads , highways , airports , buildings .
你需要吸引商家他們會來聘用最先移居特別市的人們	you need to attract merchants who are going to hire the first people to migrate to the market .
你需要吸引家庭那些會來長期居住的人撫養小孩 , 供他們受教育開始他們的事業	you need to attract families who are living on a longterm basis to raise their children , to get them educated , to start their careers .
在這樣的綱領下 , 人們會移居那裡	in this syllabus , people move there .
城市才能建立起來	cities are built .
我們還可以改善這個模型的規模	we can also improve the scale of the model .

大多數人沒有意識到這些肉眼看不到的生物微生物構成了地球約一半的生物量而所有的動物加起來也才佔地球生物量的千分之一	most of us don't realize that the microbes that are invisible make up about half the biomass of our planet , and all the animals combined make up about one thousandth of the earth's biomass .
跑到海邊喝上一口海水或許不是牛津人經常做的事但請記住每一毫升的海水裡有大約一百萬個的細菌其中的病毒更是以千萬計	getting to the beach and having a seawater maybe not what the oxford used to do , but keep in mind that there are about a million bacteria in every single milliliter of seawater , even more viruses in every single virus .

考察伊始 , 我們在百慕大進行了測試專案然後前往哈利法克斯接著到美國東海岸加勒比海、巴拿馬運河穿過加拉帕哥斯群島 , 然後橫跨太平洋現在我們正在穿越印度洋的過程中	in recognition , we did a testing project at bermudu , and then we went to harrie fas , and then we went to the east coast of caribbean , the panama river , through the galapagos , and then across the pacific , and now we're going through the indian ocean .

實驗其實非常簡單	it's a very simple experiment .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	take the seawater , filter it , gather creatures of different sizes of filters , and bring their dna back to the laboratory of roxville , where we can complete 100 million letters of genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and through that , we've made some remarkable discoveries .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , before we had one or two visual pigments in our eyes , we suggested that just one or two species in nature have one or the same visual pigment
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the upper seawater area of warm seas , almost every species has these types of light receptors and uses sunlight as a source and communication tool .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	in a single gathering point , from a single bucket of water , we find 1 . 3 million new genes , equal to 50 , 000 new species .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	by funding funding from the sloan foundation , we've already expanded our research to the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're calculating how many viruses and bacteria float around in the air we breathe every day , especially in closed environments like planes and aisles .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we've been filtered through some very simple instruments on the top of a building in new york city , and we filter out billions of microbes a day .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're now sequenced them .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	and just looking at the dataset , just in the galapagos , we found that nearly every 200 miles we see tremendous diversity in samples .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	the different gradients might be partially explaining this diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a satellite image based on temperature , showing warm regions , and the warm blue regions show cold , and we found that samples in warm water and cold water have tremendous differences in the richness of species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	the other thing that surprised us is that these photo receptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that through their amino acid sequence .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	they're also very different between regions .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	maybe not surprisingly , in the tendency of nearly blue miles , towards receptors , " to the blue light .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they're going to see a lot of green light .
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	the difference between the infrared and the ultraviolet period that travels towards the extremes may be even larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	to evaluate all of the genes that we've collected , we have summarized all of the data , including all of the data we've collected so far , representing more than half of the genetic data on the planet about 29 million genes .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we put these genes into families to try and answer: are we discovering new members of the known genome or new families of the genome ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out that we have found about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we've gained from the environment is just a linear supplement to these new genomes .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we are at the very early stages of discovering life and its components and its genetic basis .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	let's take a look at what's called an evolutionary tree , where we humans live in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	it's only about 29 million genes in the animal kingdom , and our genome is only 24 , 000 .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we count all the animals together , we share less than 3 , 000 , maybe 120 , 000 different gene families .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now , i don't just think of these genes as design components of evolution .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go from a genecentric perspective to a theory of richard dawkins , not a central genomics perspective , to think about the way these genes are constructed differently .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna over the last decade or two , somehow synchronize synchrony and cheaper .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea of the synthetic genome was in 1995 , when we sequenced the second genitalia , the genitalia .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a nice tshirt that said , " i love my genitals . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's really just a tiny , tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	they have about 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus has 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we asked the question: if one species needs 800 genes , another requires 500 of them to use one smaller set of genomes to make a smaller living system .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started making the mutations of the seats .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	transposons are short pieces of dna that randomly insert into the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert that into the gene , you disrupt the function of the gene .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we looked at all the genes that were transferred in and made these " nonnecessary genes " maps .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that the environmental impact is very critical , and we can define essential and nonnecessary , based on the conditions that the environment exists .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we're also trying to do a more intuitive study of 13 animals with related relationships , and we're trying to compare their genomes to see if they have the same set of points .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and what we found was that only 173 genes were identical in all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if we ignore a single cell messenger , this gene pool can also expand a little bit when we look at a core set of about 310 gene banks .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we think , from the minimum of 500 gene expansions , condense , or shrink , determine what you're looking at , to about 300 to 400 genes .
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to construct a chromosome based on these genes , and we have to do it based on the framework .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	and what we found was that the big exact specification of synthetic dna is very , very difficult .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague , hanm smith and claire harchanson , invented an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a virus with 5 , 000 base pairs in just two weeks , and has a hundred percent accuracy in the genome sequence and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it's a pretty exciting experiment: we're just injecting dna fragments of synthetic dna into bacteria , and all of a sudden , the synthesis of the viral pellets , and the viruses are killing the bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	this isn't the first synthetic virus that had been made about a year ago , and this is the only one percent active virus that was made , it took about three years to synthesize .

有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	some people immediately started worrying about the threat of biological weapons , and not long ago , i was at the senate committee and another specific committee evaluated by the u . s . government .
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	i think the most important thing to remember is the fact that people , as opposed to the images that things have happened .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	basically , any virus that has been sequenced now , the genome can be synthesized .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were immediately frightened of things like ebola or smallpox , but the dna extracted from these organisms was not contagious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even though someone made the smallpox virus genome , the dna itself did not cause infections .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security sector really needs to worry about the designer's virus .
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , the united states and the former soviet union , have spent an enormous effort on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	if these studies are truly ending , the odds of having manufactured designer viruses in the future are pretty slim .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think it's possible to create singlecelled organisms within two years .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the true nucleus , the ones we own , can also be made within a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can divide into this artificial genome , framework and different genes , and allow us to construct dozens of different structures .

例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for example , from the third species we sequenced , methanoccus bacterium , which is the equivalent of high temperature at the water boiling point , hydrogen as a energy source and depending on co2 to provide its own carbon for the environment .

那什麼是時間洞察力呢 ? 這將是我下面要講的	so what is a time perspective ? that's what i'm going to tell you .
時間洞察力是研究個人包括我們在內 , 如何以時間區域或時間類別為單位劃分自身的經歷體驗 。	time perspective is the study of individuals , including us , including dividing our experiences into time zones and time categories .
其實我們一直都在自然而然地做著	we've actually been doing it in a natural way .
而影響我們劃分方式的因素有很多 , 包括不同的文化背景、國家個人、社會階層以及不同的教育背景	and the parameters that affect how we scramble different cultural backgrounds , individuals , classes , different educational contexts .
問題是由於這些因素的存在 , 最終導致時間洞察力都具是片面的因為你學會經常使用其中的一些 , 而其他的則被很少使用	the problem is that the presence of these factors ultimately led to time perception , because you learn to use them constantly , and others are few .
是什麼促使你做出那些選擇 ?	what makes those choices you make ?
你所做的決定是基於你怎麼採取行動的	the decision you make is based on how you act .
對一些人來說 , 這個決定只是基於現狀另一些人是基於他們的直覺 。	for some people , this decision is just based on their intuition .
對於那些基於現狀而做決定的人我們稱呼他們為: " 面向現在 " 因為他們專注於現正發生的事情	for those of you who make decisions based on the status quo , we call them " facelessness , " because they focus on what's happening .
對於另一些人來說 , 現正發生什麼並不重要	for others , it doesn't matter what's happening .
就好像是說: " 我以前好像經歷過類似的事情 " 一樣	it's like , " i used to feel like i've been through this before . "
所以 , 他們基於過去的經驗來做決定	so they make decisions based on the past experience .
我們稱呼這些人為: " 觀望過去 " , 因為他們專注於過去	we call them " watch the past , " because they focus on the past .
還有一部分人 , 他們的考慮不是基於現在 , 也不是過去而是未來	and then there's a group of people who don't take into account the present , not the past , but the future .

我們稱呼這些人為:展望未來 。 因為他們專注於將來會是怎麼樣的	we call those people the future , because they're focused on what's going to be .

那你就具有某種程度上的片面的時間洞察力	so you have a degree of insight .
實際上是有六種時間洞察力 , 其中兩個屬於 " 面向現在 "	there are actually six types of time perspectives , two of which are facing the present .
兩個屬於 " 觀望過去 " , 還有兩個屬於 " 展望未來 "	two belong to the past , and two belongings to the future .

也可以專注於 " 享受現在 " 指的是你專注於生活中的快樂 , 或者自身宿命這些都無所謂 , 因為你的生活盡在掌握	or you can focus on enjoying the present , where you focus on the joy of life , or the destiny of your own life , doesn't matter , because your life is on its hands .
當然 , 你也可以 " 展望未來 " , 設定一個目標	and of course , you can set an objective into the future .

任何時間洞察力中總是負性多於正性的	any given time perspective is more negative than just positive .

每當我聽到這個問題就感到為難因為這時我往往才從中東工作回來在那裡我的工作是拍攝幾十位巴勒斯坦人他們透過非暴力的手段保衛土地和水資源免受以色列士兵和定居者的剝奪	every time i hear that question , i find it hard , because that's when i tend to return to work in the middle east , and my job is to photograph dozens of palestinians who are stripped away from israeli soldiers and settlers who are nonviolent .
這些領導人正在努力組織一場全國範圍的大規模非暴力運動來結束侵佔在這個地區建和平	these leaders are working to organize a massive and nonviolent movement across the country to end the invasion of peace in this region .
然而大多數人可能從來沒有聽說過他們	and yet , most of us have probably never heard of them .
真相與外界猜想之間的隔閡就是關鍵原因之一解釋為何巴勒斯坦和平抵抗運動尚未取得成功	the disconnect between the truth and the outside world is one of the key reasons why the palestinian peaceful resistance has not yet acquired success .
我今天來談論的是關注的力量你們的關注的力量以及約旦河西岸加沙地帶和其它地方非暴力運動的興起和發展而今天我案例分析的主角是巴勒斯坦	i'm here to talk about the power of concentration , the power of your attention , and the rise and development of the west bank , the west bank , and other places , nonviolent movements , and today , my main character analysis is palestine .
我認為非暴力運動的成長最欠缺的並不是讓巴勒斯坦人開始進行非暴力運動而是讓我們開始關注那些早已開始非暴力運動的人	i think the growing lack of nonviolent movement is the lack of palestinians to start nonviolent movements , but let's start looking at people who are already beginning to be nonviolent .
請容我帶領你們進入這個村莊來解釋這個道理這個村莊叫佈德魯斯	please let me take you into this village and explain that this is a village called turus .
大約七年前這裡的人們面臨著滅頂之災以色列宣佈它將築起一堵圍牆而其中一段將跨過這個村莊	about seven years ago , the folks here were facing the peak , israel announced it would build a wall , and one of them would cross the village .
村民將失去40%的土地並被包圍起來失去從這裡進入約旦河西岸地區的自由	the villagers would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded by losing freedom from the west bank .
在當地領導人的激勵下他們發動了一場和平抵抗運動以避免發生這樣的結果	inspired by the local leaders , they launched a peaceful resistance movement to prevent the outcome .
我給大家播放影片的一些片斷讓你們大致瞭解實地發生的情況	so i'm going to show you a couple of snippets of film to give you an idea of what's happening in the field .
巴勒斯坦女子:他們說那堵圍牆會將巴勒斯坦和以色列分隔開來	lady palestine: they said that the wall would block palestine from israel .
在佈德魯斯我們意識到那堵牆會搶佔我們的土地	in bedrus , we realized that the wall would take over our lands .
以色列男子:這堵圍牆事實上是防止恐怖行動的一項解決方法	israeli man: the wall is actually a solution to preventing terrorism .
今天我號召大家加入一場和平的遊行	today i'm calling you to a peaceful march .
與你們並肩行動的是幾十位以色列兄弟姊妹	working side by side with you are the ten israeli brothers and sisters .
以色列行動主義者:最令軍隊害怕的就是非暴力抵抗	israeli activist: the most terrifying troops are nonviolent resistance .
女子:我們看到男人們試圖推開那些士兵但是沒有人成功	woman: we see men trying to push those soldiers , but nobody succeeded .
而我認為姑娘們能夠做到	and i think girls can do that .
法塔赫組織成員:我們必須清空頭腦中傳統的觀念	fatah members: we have to clear the traditions of our minds .
哈馬斯組織成員:我們是完全和平的我們希望讓它遍及整個巴勒斯坦	hamas formed members: we were completely peaceful , and we wanted it to spread all over the palestines .
口號聲:團結一致的民族	slogan: solidarity .
法塔赫哈馬斯人民陣線	the fatahmas route .
新聞主播:圍牆附近的衝突仍在繼續	news anchor: the conflict around the wall continues .
記者:以色列邊警受命驅逐抗議人群	interviewer: israeli cops deported protesters .
他們被允許採用一切必要的強制手段	they're allowed to adopt the necessary mandatory techniques .
男子:他們正在開火	man: they're fired .
這裡就像費盧傑到處是槍聲	it's like a gunshot all over the place .
以色列行動主義者:我知道我們是去送死	israeli activist: i know we're dead .
但是我身邊的許多人沒有一絲畏懼	but a lot of people around me didn't fear .
以色列士兵:一場非暴力抗議無法阻止我們建立這堵牆	israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest did not stop us from building the wall .
抗議者:這是一場和平的示威遊行	protesters: this is a peaceful demonstration .
我們不需要使用暴力	we don't need to use violence .
口號聲:我們必勝我們必勝	chanting: we're going to win .
朱莉婭•帕夏:當我第一次聽說佈德魯斯的這段故事我感到非常驚訝全球媒體居然沒有報道在2003年也就是七年以前所發生的這一系列了不起的事件	julia pasha: when i first heard about this story of druid russe , i was surprised that there was no newspaper in 2003 , this series of remarkable events that happened seven years ago .
而更令人吃驚的是佈德魯斯最終取得了勝利	and what was even more surprising was that the sandrus eventually won .
經過長達10個月的和平抵抗運動那裡的居民說服了以色列政府將圍牆從他們的土地遷出轉而遷到綠線上也就是國際公認的巴以領土分界線上	over a decade of peaceful resistance , the residents convinced the israeli governments to move the wall from their lands and to the green line , the international recognition border of babel territory .
佈德魯斯的抵抗運動的影響從此遍及約旦河西岸的所有村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的巴勒斯坦人居住區	the effects of broadrus against resistance have since spread to all the villages in the west bank and palestinian residential neighborhoods in jerusalem .
然而媒體對這些事件幾乎隻字未提	but the media has remained virtually remarkable in these events .
這種漠視給巴勒斯坦非暴力運動的成長甚至生存產生了沉重的打擊	the growth of this survival to the palestinian nonviolent movement has even survived a heavy battle .
暴力抵抗和非暴力抵抗有一個非常重要的共同點兩者像一個劇院渴望吸引觀眾的青睞	violence resistance and nonviolence resistance have a very important commonality , like a theater longing to attract audiences .
如果暴力演員總是領銜主演將全球目光聚焦巴勒斯坦問題那麼非暴力領導人就很難向他們的民眾證明和平的反抗才是帶他們脫離苦海的可行方案	if violence actors are constantly dominating the world's focus on the palestinian problem , it's very hard for nonviolent leaders to prove peaceful rebellion to their people that it's possible to take them out of the suffering sea .
在座為人父母的估計對關注的力量並不陌生	an estimated estimate of the power of attention as a parent is no stranger .
如果孩子第一次鬧脾氣就得到父母的注意那麼你的孩子以後肯定會鬧得更厲害	if your child tantrums for the first time , gets a parent's attention , then your child will definitely be haunted for it .
鬧脾氣就會成為兒童心理學家所說的功能性行為孩子學會用這種方式引起父母的注意	distletion will become what children's call functional behavior , which their parents learn to pay attention to .
父母可以透過關注或不予理睬來鼓勵或抑制此行為	parents can encourage or inhibit the behavior without paying attention or care .
而這也適用於成年人	and this also applies to adults .
事實上社群和國家的行為是能夠受到影響而改變的而這取決於國際社會選擇關注的方面	in fact , the behavior of the community and the behavior of the country depends on the international community's concerns .
我相信解決中東地區的衝突給這裡帶來和平關鍵是我們要透過更多地關注當地的非暴力領袖來把非暴力行動轉變為一種功能性行為	i believe the key to solving conflict in the middle east is that we need to transform nonviolent action into a functional behavior by paying more attention to local concerns .
在約旦河西岸加沙地帶以及東耶路撒冷地區拍攝那裡的村莊時我親眼目睹了區區一部紀錄片對行為轉變所帶來的影響	when i shot villages in the rivery gaza and in the west coast of jerusalem , i saw firsthand the effects of a documentary shift in a district .
在離耶路撒冷很近的一個名叫瓦拉傑的村子那裡的村民面臨著與佈德魯斯相似的困境	in the village near jerusalem , a village called valagraja , where the villagers are faced with trouble similar to russ .
他們即將被包圍起來失去大片土地無法自由進入約旦河西岸或耶路撒冷	they're going to be surrounded , they're going to lose large pieces of land , they can't be free from the west bank or jerusalem
在進行了長達兩年的非暴力抵抗之後他們最終心灰意冷因為他們沒有得到任何人的注意	after two years of nonviolent resistance , they finally discouraged , because they didn't get their attention .
於是我們在那裡組織播放了紀錄片	so there we were organizing , you know , documentaries .
一週之後他們組織了一場在當時參與人數最多最有紀律的遊行示威	and a week later , they organized a demonstration that was involved in most disciplined marches .
組織者們說當村民在紀錄片中看到佈德魯斯的故事他們感覺到確實有人與他們志同道合人們是在乎的	the organizers said that when the villagers saw the story of verderus in the documentary , they felt that there was indeed sync with their volunteers , that people cared .
於是他們沒有放棄	so they didn't give up .
以色列有一個新的和平運動被稱為 " 索裡德拉爾特 " 在希伯來語中意為 " 團結一致 "	israel has a new movement of peace , known as the solidarity , which means " unity " in hebrew .
佈德魯斯的故事成為了這個運動的領導者招兵買馬的主要手段之一	the story of budrus became one of the leaders of this movement recruiting soldiers for horses .
他們反映說那些從未加入任何運動的以色列人看了紀錄片之後瞭解了非暴力抵抗的力量並開始加入他們行動	they reflected that the israelis who had never joined a movement , watched a documentary , realized the power of nonviolent resistance and began to join them .
瓦拉傑和索裡德拉爾特運動的例子告訴我們即使是小成本的獨立電影也能夠幫助非暴力抵抗轉變為一種功能性行為	the examples of vagra and the solydrall movement have shown us that even a tiny , independent film can help nonviolent resistance to a functional behavior .
想象一下主流媒體若是開始報道每週在貝拉因尼亞林瓦拉傑等村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的香克哈拉和西路萬巴勒斯坦居住區裡發生的非暴力示威活動這將產生多麼巨大的力量更多的人會關注非暴力運動領導者重視他們讓他們的工作更有成效	imagine the mainstream media that starts reporting every week in the villages like belaina lynn vager , and in the case of jerusalem , cikhara and the palestinian residence of nonviolence that's occurring in palestinian regions , and it's going to be so much more people who care about nonviolent movement leaders and make their jobs so much more effective .
我相信最重要的是我們要認識到如果我們不關注這些運動它們就是隱形的彷彿從來沒有發生過	and i think most importantly , we have to recognize that if we don't focus on these movements , they are invisible , like they've never happened before .
但我以親身經歷為證如果我們關注這些運動就會得到發展	but i proved firsthand that these movements will develop if we care about them .
它們一旦發展其影響力就會遍及巴以衝突	once they develop their influence , they spread over battle conflict .
這種影響能夠最終將衝突化解	this conflict ultimately resolves conflict .
這些領導者證明了非暴力運動在佈德魯斯這樣的地方是可行的	these leaders have shown that nonviolent movements are doable in places like dres .
我們一起來關注他們讓他們證明這在任何地方都是可行的	let's look at them , let's make them prove that this is possible anywhere .
西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simone stonehenk uses a simple but shocking model to illustrate the league power of the inspirational leadership , which at its heart is a golden circle , which means the fundamental root of the leader's quality is answering apple , martin luther king and the wright brother’s success as an example of the typical failure of tijuan frame enjoyment , although recently it’s struggling with the missing strategy .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	but bullseye , entrepreneur , waste , sales , selling , success .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	sb: how great leaders can inspire action .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	how can you explain things when things are developing surprisingly ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , what do you explain when people seem to have succeeded unexpectedly ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why is apple so innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	over the years and years , year after year , they've become more innovative than all the competitors .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're actually just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they're no different from the other companies .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	it's the same approach to the same talent , the same business , consultant and media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem to be a little bit different ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	similarly , why is it that martin luther king came to lead the civil rights movement ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	at that time , before the civil rights movement , he wasn't just one person , he wasn't the only great orator of the time .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	why did the white brothers make motivated manned vehicles and seem more capable compared to them , compared to other teams .
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they didn't create manned airplanes , and the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there has to be something else that's going on .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	about three and a half years ago , i made a discovery .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	this discovery completely changed the way in which i thought about how the world works , and even fundamentally changed the way in which i work life .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's when i discovered a pattern .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i find that all the great leaders and organizations of the world , whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers , they think , act and communicate exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but the opposite is the opposite of what everyone else does .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i've done is to organize it , and it's probably the simplest concept in the world .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? how ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why organizations and leaders can trigger inspiration and potential where other people can't .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	let me explain these terms as quickly as possible .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	everybody on the planet understands what they do , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , you can call your differences , or your unique craftsmanship , or your unique selling points , or whatever to say .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations understood why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	it's okay with the " why " and " profit . "
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	profit is just one outcome , always only one outcome .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	and i'm talking about why: what is your purpose ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what's the reason why you do that ? what are your beliefs ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why does your organization exist ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why did you get out of bed every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why should anyone care ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	it turns out that the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is inward .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	clearly , the way we start with clarity and then with ambiguity .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but inspiring leaders and organizations , wherever they scale , they think and act and communicate from the inside out .
舉個例子吧 。	let's take an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i showed apple because it's a simple example , and everybody understands it .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple were like any other company , their marketing information would be this: " we make the best computers .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design beauty , use simple , interface friendly .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	would you like to buy one ? " not so much .
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	this is how most of us communicate .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	it's also the way that most markets communicate with each other , the way most of us communicate .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our profession is doing , we say how we're remarkably different , or how we're better than other people , and then we expect other people's reactions , like buying , like voting , etc .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	this is our new law firm , and we have the best lawyers and biggest clients , and we can always satisfy our clients' demands .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new vehicle , very efficient , leather seat . buy a car .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" every single thing we do to break out and innovate .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we firmly believe we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	the way we challenge the status quo is by designing our products very beautifully , using simplicity and interface friendship .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we're just making the best computer in the process .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	want to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	it feels totally different , right ? you're going to buy one from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	all i did was reverse the sequence of conveying information .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	as it turns out , people are buying something that you're not making , and people are buying your beliefs and missions .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products that you make ; people buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	that explains why everybody here , from apple , came to mind when they bought a computer from apple .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but when we bought an mp3 player from apple , cell phones , digital cameras feel comfortable .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and in fact , as i said earlier , apple is just a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	nothing splits apples from structured competition .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competitors and apple have the same capacity to make all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	in fact , they tried it as well .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , czech released the flatscreen tv .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they're very capable of making flatscreen tv .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	they've been working on a padding display for many years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	the dar was launching an mp3 player and a palmpilot , and their product was very good , the design of the product was good , but nobody bought them .
其實 , 說到這裡 , 我們無法想象會從戴爾公司買mp3播放器 。	in fact , speaking here , we can't imagine buying an mp3 player from dar .
你為什麼會從一家電腦公司買mp3播放器呢 ?	why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?
但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products that you make ; people buy your beliefs .
做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	the goal of the company is not to do business with everybody who wants your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's about having a business with those who have the same ideas .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	this is the most amazing part . none of these are my own perspectives .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	all of these ideas are rooted in biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	it's not psychology , it's biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the horizontal screens of the brain , you'll see that there are actually three major parts of the human brain that are actually very well matched with golden circles .
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our latest brain , the jurisdictional brain , or our cerebral cortex , corresponds to what is the circle .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the cortex is responsible for all of our rational and logical thinking and language .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two sections in the middle are our two brains , and the brain is responsible for all of our emotions , such as trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's responsible for all behaviors and decisionmaking , but it doesn't have a language .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we're extroverted , yes , people can understand a lot of complex information , like features , facts and graphs .
但不足以激發行動 。	but not enough to inspire action .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're having introverts , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we're rationally thinking about what we say and do .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	that's the source of the decision that comes from the heart .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show people all the data charts , and they say , " i know what the data and the graph means , but it just doesn't feel right . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use the verb , the feeling , right ?
因為控制決策的那一部分大腦並不支配語言 ,	because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't govern language .
我們只好說 " 我不知道為什麼 , 就是感覺不對 。 "	we just said , " i don't know why , it just feels wrong . "
或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or sometimes you listen to the call from the heart , or listen to the soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to break these ideas down too thoroughly , but hearts and souls are not part of control .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this happens in your brain , controlling decisionmaking , not language .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you do what you do , and people react to your motivations , then how do you possibly win people's support from you , from where you buy things , or , more importantly , loyalty to you and want to be a part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	and again , the goal is not just to sell things to people who need them ; it's to sell them to people who share your beliefs .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to employ those who need a job ; the goal is to employ those who share faith .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say that if you hire someone who just works because they can do this job , they just work for you , but if you hire people who share your beliefs , they will pay you hot , sweat and tears for you .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	now , there's no more appropriate example than the white brothers' story .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	most of you have never heard of samuel langley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion for putting into an aircraft was like the hot website of the day .
每個人都在做嘗試 。	everyone's trying .
塞繆爾•蘭利擁有所有大家認為是成功的要素 。	samuel lanley has all the ingredients that people consider to be successful .
我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or your company fail ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people are using the same three things to answer you , lack of funding , bad people , bad shape .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	it's always those three reasons , so let's go ahead and analyze them .
國防部給了塞繆爾•蘭利5萬美金作為研製飛行器的資金 。	the department of defense funded the samuel lanley 50 , 000 dollars as a r&amp ; d robot .
所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so money isn't a problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he's worked at harvard , and he's worked at the smithsonian , and he's got a lot of connections , and he knows the best people at the time .
因此 , 他僱傭了用資金能吸引到的最優秀的人才 。 當時的市場形勢相當有利 。	so he employs the best people he can attract , and that was a fairly good market shape .
紐約時報對他做跟蹤報道 , 每個人都支援他 。	the new york times reported and tracked him , and everybody supported him .
但是為什麼你們連聽都沒聽說過他呢 ?	but why have you never heard of him before ?
與此同時 , 幾百公里之外的俄亥俄州代頓市有一對兄弟 , 奧維爾•萊特和維爾伯•萊特 , 他們倆沒有任何我們認為的成功的要素 。	meanwhile , hundreds of kilometers away in newton , ohio , there's a brother , orville wright and virgin wright , who don't have any elements of what we think of as success .
他們沒有錢 。 他們用腳踏車店的收入來追求他們的夢想 。 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有一個人上過大學 , 就連奧維爾和維爾伯也沒有 。 紐約時報更是不沾邊的 。	they didn't have any money . they used bicycle store income to pursue their dreams . none of the wright brothers had gone to college , even avel and walber . the new york times had more to do with it .
不同的是 , 奧維爾和維爾伯追求的是一個事業 , 一個目標 , 一種信念 。	the difference is that orville and verbal are for a business , a goal , a belief .
他們相信如果他們能研製出飛行器 , 將會改變全世界的發展程序 。	they believed that if they could build robots , they would change the course of development in the world .
塞繆爾•蘭利就不同了 ,	samuel lanley was different .
他想要發財 , 他想要成名 。	he wants to make money , he wants to be famous .
他追求的是最終結果 ,	what he was looking for was the end result .
是變得富有 。	it's becoming rich .
看吧 , 看接下來怎麼樣了 。	see what's going on .
那些懷有和懷特兄弟一樣夢想的人跟他們一起熱血朝天地奮鬥著 。	those people who were preserved as white brothers , they were struggling with their blood .
另一邊的人則是為了工資而工作 。	the other side works for pay .
後來流傳的故事說 , 每次懷特兄弟出去實驗時 , 都必須帶著五組零件 , 因為那是在他們回來吃晚飯之前將要墜毀的次數 。	and the story goes that every time the white brothers get out , they have to carry all those five sets of parts , because that's how many times they're going to crash before they return to dinner .
最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 懷特兄弟成功起飛 , 但是當時沒有任何其他人在場目睹 。	finally , on december 17th , 1903 , the white brothers took off , but nobody else was there .
我們是在幾天後才知道的 。	we didn't know it until a few days later .
後來的事情進一步證實了蘭利動機不純 , 他在懷特兄弟成功的當天就辭職了 。	the event proved even further that the langley incentive had resigned on the day the white brothers were successful .
他本來應該可以說: " 夥計們 , 這真是一項偉大的發明 , 我可以改進你們的技術 。 " 但是他沒有 ,	he was supposed to be able to say , " guys , this is a great invention , i can improve your technology , " but he didn't .
因為他不是第一個製造出飛機的人 , 他就不會變得富有 , 他也不會變得有名 , 所以他辭職了 。	because he wasn't the first person to make a plane , he wouldn't be rich , he wouldn't become famous , so he quit .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	it's not your product ; it's your belief .
如果你講述你的信念 , 你將吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人 。	if you talk about your beliefs , you're going to attract people who share the same beliefs as you .
但是為什麼吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人非常重要呢 ?	but why is it so important to attract people who share the same beliefs ?
創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	innovation spreads on a regular basis , and if you don't know the pattern , you must understand the concept .
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	two and a half percent of our society are innovators .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	thirteen and a half percent were some of the early adopters .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	the next 34% are the most accepted earlier , and then the vast majority and final action later accepted .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	the people who ended up acting on the cell phone were the only reason they could not buy a dial on the phone anymore .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	and although we're at various places on this curve at different times , the pattern of innovation tells us that if you want to have a success in the public market , or you have to have an idea for the public that's 15 to 18 percent of the market reception , then the markets really started .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask the company , " what about your new business ? "
他們會很自豪地告訴你 " 哦 , 大概有10%吧 。 "	they'll tell you proudly , " oh , it's about 10 percent . "
是呀 , 你有可能就在10%的顧客群這裡過不去了 。	yeah , you might be here with 10 percent of the customers .
我們都能讓10%的人 " 意會 " ,	we can all get 10 percent of the population " meaning . "
對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , we describe them like that .
就好比描述那種感覺: " 哦 , 他們有點心領神會了 " 。	it's like describing that feeling: " oh , they're slightly in charge of god . "
問題是:你怎麼在他們還沒有成為你的顧客之前就發現那些能意會的人 , 和那些不能意會的人 ?	the question is: how do you find people who intend to be your customers before they've become your customers ?
這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	this is the problem , and this is the gap that you need to fill in , as geoffrey murmill said , the gap to cross , because most of you wouldn't try new things in the early days , unless somebody had tried it first .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these people , the innovators and the early few , they like the bold attempts .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they do things more naturally intuitively , in their view of the world , not just because of what products there are in the market .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	this is a batch of people who came to the iphone the first couple of days to stand up waiting six hours to buy , and in fact , you could just walk into the store in a week or so .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a group of people who bought a $40 , 000 bought at the time of the flatscreen tv , although the technology at the time hadn't really matured .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and by addition , they're not buying them because of the technological advancements , but for themselves .
因為他們想成為第一個體驗新產品的人 。	because they want to be the first to experience a new product .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你的行動只是證明了你的信念 。	people are not buying your product ; people are buying your beliefs ; your actions are just proving your beliefs .
實際上 , 人們會去做能夠體現他們的信念的事情 。	people actually do things that reflect their beliefs .
那些為了搶先在頭六個小時內買到iphone而排六個小時的隊的人 , 是出於他們的世界觀 , 出於他們想別人怎麼看自己 。 他們是第一批體驗者 。	those six hours of queue bought the iphone in the first six hours , the worldviews , out of their views , were the first group of people to see themselves .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 他們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy your product ; they buy your beliefs .
我再舉些著名的例子吧 , 證實創新傳播規律的一個失敗的例子和一個成功的例子 。	let me give you some famous examples of how innovation can propagate a failed example of the spread of innovation and a successful example .
首先我們講這個失敗的例子 。	first of all , let's start with this failure .
還是商業上的 。	or commercial .
就如我們一秒鐘前剛剛說過的 , 成功的要素是充足的資金 , 優秀的人才和良好的市場形勢 。 那麼 , 是不是如果有這些你就應該獲得成功 。	as we just said a second ago , success is about financing , good talent and good marketplaces , and if you have success , if you have success .
自從推出蒂沃機頂盒以來 , 大概是八、九年前 , 直到今天 , 它們一直是市場上唯一的最高品質的產品 , 這沒有任何異議 。	they have been the single highest quality product in the market since they launched the top box , probably eight or nine years ago , until today .
它們絕對是資金充足 ,	they're absolutely funded .
市場形勢也大好 。	it's also a fantastic market shape .
其實 , " 蒂沃 " 都變成了一個日常用的動詞 。	in fact , tiva became a daily verb .
比如:我經常把東西蒂沃到我那臺華納數碼影片錄影機裡面 。	for instance: i used to get something to my warner's digital video camera .
但是蒂沃是個商業上的失敗案例 ,	but tijuya is a business failure .
他們沒有賺到一分錢 。	they didn't make a penny .
他們上市時 , 股票價格大約在30到40美元 , 然後就直線下跌 , 而成交價格從沒超過10美元 。	when they came to market , the stock price was about 30 to 40 dollars , and the stock price fell down in a stock line , and the price was never more than 10 dollars .
實際上 , 我印象中它的交易價格從來沒有超過6美元 , 除了幾次小的震盪之外 。	in fact , there was never more than six dollars a trade price in my impression except for a few tiny concussions .
因為你會發現 , 蒂沃公司新推出他們的產品時 , 他們只是告訴我們他們產品是什麼 ,	because what you find is that when tijuv is launching their products , they're just telling us what their product is .
他們說 " 我們的產品可以把電視節目暫停 , 跳過廣告 , 回放電視節目 , 還能記住你的觀看習慣 , 你甚至都不用刻意設定它 。 "	they said , " our product pauses , skips commercials , tv shows , and you have to remember your rituals , and you don't even have to construct them intentionally . "
挑剔的人們說: " 我們不相信你 ,	people who are picky say , " we don't believe in you .
我們不需要這樣的東西 , 我們也不喜歡這樣的東西 。	we don't need to have this kind of stuff , we don't like it .
你在唬人 。 "	you're bugging people . "

如果海馬區出現損傷 , 像老年痴呆症患者一樣 , 你將喪失記憶力 , 乃至記不起將車停在了何處 。	if there's damage to the hippocampus , like someone with alzheimer's , you lose your memory , and you can't remember where the car is .
hippocampus這個詞源自拉丁語 , 有 " 海馬 " 之意因為腦中海馬區的形狀看上去有點像 " 海馬 " 。	the word " hippocampus " comes from the latin word " hippocampus , " because the shape of the hippocampus looks a little bit like the hippocampus .
海馬區和大腦其它區域的組成相似 , 都由神經元構成 。	the hippocampus is similar to the rest of the brain , all made of neurons .
人的大腦由大約一千億個神經元細胞組成 。	the human brain consists of about 100 billion neurons .
每個神經元細胞之間透過一些連線中介互相傳送小的電脈衝或者尖峰電壓來進行 " 交流 " 。	each neuron communicates a small electrical pulse in some of the connections , or multiple multiple hybrids .
海馬區由兩層片狀的細胞群構成 , 這兩層細胞群緊密相連 。	the hippocampus is made of two decks of cells , and these two layers are intimately connected .
科學家們透過記錄老鼠在某環境中搜羅食物時其腦中單個神經元細胞的反應來了解 " 空間記憶 " 的工作原理與工作機制 。	scientists respond to the response of a single neuron in their brain by recording the work and the work mechanisms of spatial memory .

癲癇病患者有時需要監測他們的腦電活動情況 。	patients with epilepsy sometimes need to monitor their brain activity .
一些患者玩一種電子遊戲 , 遊戲中他們在一個小鎮上自由開車 。	some patients play a video game where they're driving freely in a small town .
然後當他們驅車駛過鎮上的某一處時 , 他們大腦海馬區中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 便會被啟用 , 發出訊號 。	and then when they drive across town somewhere , the neurons in the hippocampus will be initiated , sending signals .
那麼這 " 定位細胞 " 是怎麼知道老鼠或人處於某個位置的呢 ?	so how does a given cell know where a mouse or a human is ?
這裡有兩個神經元細胞 , 它們告訴我們 , 在定位時環境的邊界是至關重要的 。	there are two neurons here , and they tell us that the boundaries of the positioning environment are essential .
上面的這個細胞傾向於在老鼠向盒子中部走去時產生訊號 。	the cell at the top tends to generate signals when the cell walks in the middle of the box .
因此當你將盒子擴大 , 相應的訊號活躍區也隨之擴大 。	so when you expand the boxes , the signals that correspond to that area expand .

因為所有的網狀訊號集合體都有相同的對稱軸 , 以及相同的網格朝向 , 這裡以橘紅色標識 , 這就意味著大腦中特定部位的所有網狀細胞的聯網行為的變化應該取決於我們是在向著這六個方向運動還是沿著六個方向之間所夾的某一個方向運動 。	because the collection of grid signals has the same symmetrical axis and the same grid's direction , shown here in orange red , that means that all the changes in the brain that are specific to the network behavior depending on whether we're moving along these six directions or whether we're moving along the six direction .

現在我們回頭看看荷馬 。	now let's go back to homer .

或許車已經被拖走了 ,	maybe the car's been dragged .

撇開 " 空間記憶力 " 而言 , 倘若我們單獨觀察這種網狀訊號集在整個大腦中的活動情況 , 就會發現這種訊號形式分佈廣泛 , 每當我們需要回憶一些自己過去的經歷時這種網狀的訊號形式就會活躍起來 , 譬如 , 當你試圖回憶上次參加婚禮的情況時	now , despite spatial memory , if we just observe the activity of these signals all over the brain , we find that this signal is widely distributed when we need to recall some of our experiences of the past , for example , when you try to recall engage in a wedding situation .

好了 , 以上就是在認知神經科學領域所開闢的新紀元 , 在這個領域中 , 我們開始嘗試從大腦中數以億計的單個神經元細胞的行為出發 , 來了解人類心理活動產生的過程 。 比如人們是如何記憶、想象甚至思考的	now , this is a new era of cognitive neuroscience , where we're beginning to try and understand the behavior of individual neurons in the brain hundreds of millions of neurons in the brain , how human psychological activities are produced .

但你知道 , 生活不是開關 。	but you know , life is not a switch .

在結束時 , 我想說在今天早些時候聽到的關於維基百科的一些東西 。 我經常用維基百科查一些東西 , 就像你所知道的 , 維基百科不是靠12個聰明的人把自己關在屋子裡寫文章建立的 。	so in closing , i want to say something i heard earlier today about wikipedia , and i use wikipedia a lot , as you know , wikipedia is not built by 12 smart people in the room writing articles .
維基百科是靠每天數萬人的更新 , 數百萬人的提取資訊而建立的 。	wikipedia is built by tens of thousands of people renewing every day , millions of people extracting information .
這完美的說明了沒有一個人能比共同思考更聰明 。	and that perfectly suggests that no one of us can think together as smart as all of us .
沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 能有我們共同思考更睿智 。	none of us , no one alliance , no one country , has the brilliant wisdom of all of us thinking together .
維基百科的宣言很簡單:建立一個能人人自由共享所有知識的世界 。	wikipedia's manifesto was simple: a world freely available to everyone .
